MURIEL BOWSER
MAYOR
April 14, 2026
The Honorable Phil Mendelson, Chairman
Council of the District of Columbia
1350 Pennsylvania Avenue, NW
Washington, DC 20004
Dear Chairman Mendelson:
On behalf of the more than 700,000 residents of Washington, DC, I am pleased to submit to the Council of
the District of Columbia my Fiscal Year 2027 Proposed Budget and Financial Plan, Grow DC.1 This
budget reflects our resilience, our values, and our continued commitment to building a stronger, safer,
and more vibrant city.
It's worth repeating that Washington, DC is a world-class city, delivering first-class services and
projects to our residents. We have the number one park system in the nation; built 36,000 new homes in
less than five years; lead the nation in office-to-residential conversions; have the fastest improving urban
school district; and have driven down crime to its lowest levels in at least three decades. And last year,
we secured the city's largest private investment with the announcement that our Washington Commanders
would come back home to a new RFK Stadium.
With this budget we remain laser focused on growing our local economy. Before the COVID-19
pandemic, the city's economic growth was predictable. We had a fast-growing population and strong
downtown demand that led to steady revenue growth which allowed us to expand our programs and
services. However, this is not the economy we have today. While our population is still growing-that
growth is happening slowly-widespread teleworking continues to strain our commercial office
market, and federal job losses have impacted thousands of District households, all of which contribute to
slower revenue growth. The Grow DC budget faces these new economic realities head on so that we can
continue growing our economy and delivering world-class city services.
Investing in High-Quality Education
Our years of investing in public education have delivered results our city can be proud of--our highest
ever graduation rate, continued enrollment gains, and great schools in all eight wards. That's why the
1 Included in this submission are the Fiscal Year 2027 Local Budget Act of 2026, the Fiscal Year 2027 Federal Portion
Budget Request Act of 2026, and the Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026. In addition, I am submitting the
following accompanying measures: the Fiscal Year 2026 Revised Local Budget Emergency Act of 2026, the Fiscal
Year 2025 Revised Local Budget Temporary Act of 2026, and the Fiscal Year 2026 Revised Local Budget Emergency
Declaration Resolution of 2026.

Grow DC budget increases the Uniform Per Student Funding Formula by 2.55 percent, bringing the
foundation level to$15,455 perstudent, andsupportsnearly 100,000public andpublic charter students.
We are expanding the Advanced Technical Centers, which give our high school students hands-on
career and technical education, and we are expanding high-impact tutoring to help more students
recover and grow academically.
The Grow DC budget provides continued support to the DC Futures Program? to ensure residents
pursuing degrees at the University ofthe District ofColumbia (UDC) can finish their programs. Our
six-year capi tal plan includes more than $2 bi llion to modernize public school facilities, upgrade
technology, and support improvements at UDC, including funds necessary to unlock its first-ever
student housingthrough a public-private partnership.
Continuing Historie Progress in Public Safety
We have made significant progress in driving down crime since it spiked in 2023, resulting in the
Jowest amountofviolentcrime inatleast 30 years. The Grow DCbudgetbuilds on this momentum by
ensuring MPD has the resources to hire, recruit, and retain officers, while alsosupporting full funding
for the Fire and Emergency Medical Services Department, Office of Unified Communications,
Department of Corrections, Department of Forensic Sciences, and other core agencies in our public
safetyecosystem.
We are investing more than $500 million in our six-year capital plan to modernize public safety
facilities, purchase new firetrucks and ambulances, replace aging and outdated equipment, increase
housing capacity at our juvenile justice facilities, and upgrade critical communications and public
safety technologyso our first responders have the toolsthey need to help keep us safe.
Growing Our Local Economy and Making It Easierto Do Business
To keep DC competitive and ensure the city’s strong economic future, the Grow DC budget reduces
the cost ofdoing business by lowering business-related fees, supports major redevelopment projects
through targeted incentives, and continues to invest in grant programs to help our small businesses
thrive.
Wecontinue todiversify oureconomy throughthe Vitality Fund’, the Tech Ecosystem Fund‘, andnew
housing tax abatements to encourage produc t ion of moderate-income, “missing middle” housing. We
are also investing significantly inthe revitalization of Downtown and unlocking underutilized spaces
citywide—from Hill East to Poplar Point to the RFKcampus.
Expanding Health Care Access and Supporting Residents in Need
Nearlyfour inten DCresidentsdependon ourMedicaid, Basic Health Plan,orAlliance programs. The
Grow DC budgetmaintains comprehensive coverage while also responding to risinghealth care costs.
We are adding new dental and vision benefits for Basic Health Plan and Alliance enrollees, funding
new chip cards forourSNAP participants to help preventbenefit theft, and expanding bridge housing
and homelessness prevention programs. We are funding the replacementofkey shelter facilities and
capital improvements that support residents experiencing homelessness. And to support our seniors,

this budget protects programs and services at the Department of Aging and Community Living and
continues our investment in a new Senior Wellness Center in Ward 2.
ProtectingCorePublic Services
Residents need clean neighborhoods, reliable transportation, accessible recreation, and responsive
services. The Grow DC budget maintains strong funding for the Department of Parks and Recreation
(DPR), DC Public Libraries (DCPL), Department of Public Works, District Department of
Transportation, Department of Energy and the Environment, and Department of Motor Vehicles to
ensure reliable core public services for our residents and businesses.
We continue to support community programsoffered at DCPL and DPR, includingthe newly opened
Fort Dupont IceArena,and wearemaintaining theClean Corridorsprogram tokeepcommercial areas
safe and welcoming. To maintain ourinnovativeedge, the GrowDC budget fundsthe developmentof
digital drivers’ licenses which will let residents have secure, electronic versions of their drivers’
licenses stored in theirdigital wallets.
Major capital investments across the city will modernize recreation centers, all public libraries, and
fund planninganddesign work on the 125-acreKenilworthParkNorth, which could leadtothe creation
of a state-of-the-art destination park in Ward 7. Ourcapital plan also includes nearly $900 million to
improve major bridges and continue our work to maintain our roads, sidewalks, and alleys. We also
continue our transportation funding commitmenttsoWMATA, Capital Bikeshare, andexpanded trails,
and pedestrian networks.
Looking Forward
We have faced significant challenges over the past few years. But Washington, DC, remains strong
because ofour residents and businessesand because we have been strong stewardsoftaxpayer dollars
over the pastthree decades.
Today, focusing on growth is more important than it everwas in Washington, DC. For all the things
we love about our city—our great schools, parks, transportation, arts, culture, and restaurants—they
all require us to have robust revenues to make robust investments. For that, we need a pro-growth
budget which weare nowdelivering with Grow DC.
‘Thank you foryour continued trust and engagement.
Sipe

129 BE IT ENACTED BY THE COUNCIL OF THE DISTRICT OF COLUMBIA, That this
130 act may be cited as the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026”.
131 TITLE I. GOVERNMENT DIRECTION AND SUPPORT
132 SUBTITLE A. TELEWORK POLICIES
133 Sec. 1001. Short title.
134 This subtitle may be cited as the “Telework Policy Amendment Act of 2026”.
135 Sec. 1002. The District of Columbia Government Comprehensive Merit Personnel Act of
136 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C. Official Code § 1-601.01 et seq.), is
137 amended by adding a new section 201a to read as follows:
138 “Sec. 201a. Telework.
139 “(a) The Mayor may establish a telework policy that applies to all agencies.
140 “(b) No personnel authority or agency shall establish its own telework policy, unless
141 authorized by the Mayor, and no personnel authority or agency shall implement a telework
142 policy other than the policy established by the Mayor pursuant to subsection (a) of this section,
143 unless authorized by the Mayor.
144 “(c) At the request of the Mayor, each agency shall submit a report to the Mayor that
145 includes information on the use of telework by the agency’s employees.
6

146 “(d) The Mayor may audit agencies’ implementation of the telework policy established
147 pursuant to subsection (a) or (b) of this section and employees’ utilization of telework to ensure
148 compliance with the telework policy and this section.
149 “(e) No personnel authority or agency may enter into a collective bargaining agreement
150 that includes or requires a telework policy.
151 “(f) For the purposes of this section, the term:
152 “(1) “Agency” shall have the meaning set forth in section 301(1) and shall include
153 agencies not otherwise subject to this act, except for the Council and agencies of the legislative
154 branch of the District government.
155 “(2) “Routine telework” means a telework arrangement in which an employee is
156 authorized to telework on an ongoing basis.
157 “(3) “Situational telework” means a temporary telework arrangement in which the
158 employee is authorized to telework due to specific, temporary personal circumstances which
159 prevent the employee from working from a District government office or worksite or for another
160 specific, temporary circumstance approved by the personnel authority.
161 “(4)(A) “Telework” means an arrangement in which an employee performs
162 employment duties at their home or other location that is not a District government office or
163 worksite during hours that constitute their official tour of duty.
164 “(B) The term “telework” includes both routine telework and situational
165 telework.”.
166 “(g) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
167 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
168 rules to implement the provisions of this section.”.
7

169 SUBTITLE B. LIMITATION ON LIABILITY AGAINST THE DISTRICT
170 Sec. 1011. Short title.
171 This subtitle may be cited as the “Limitation on Liability Against the District of
172 Columbia Act of 2026”.
173 Sec. 1012. Limitation on liability for unliquidated damage claims against the District.
174 (a) The liability of the District of Columbia, including its instrumentalities, for
175 unliquidated damages to persons or property arising out of the same incident or occurrence shall
176 not exceed $500,000 regardless of the number of claimants or beneficiaries who share in the
177 award; except, that the liability of the District of Columbia for unliquidated damages to persons
178 or property arising from intentional wrongful acts or omissions shall not exceed $1 million for all
179 claims arising out of the same incident or occurrence, regardless of the number of claimants or
180 beneficiaries who share in the award.
181 (b) No portion of an award against the District for unliquidated damages to a person may
182 include noneconomic damages unless a claimant first establishes that the claimant incurred
183 reasonable and necessary medical expenses of more than $10,000 due to the act or omission of
184 the District of Columbia for which the claim is made, except in the case of an injury resulting in
185 permanent disfigurement or death or resulting from an intentional wrongful act.
186 (c) This section shall apply to all claims or causes of action against the District of
187 Columbia, including its instrumentalities, filed in any court or other tribunal of competent
188 jurisdiction on or after October 1, 2026.
189 SUBTITLE C. DISTRICT EMPLOYEE PAID PARENTAL, FAMILY, AND
190 MEDICAL LEAVE
191 Sec. 1021. Short title.
8

192 This subtitle may be cited as the “District Employee Paid Parental, Family, and Medical
193 Leave Amendment Act of 2026”.
194 Sec. 1022. The District of Columbia Government Comprehensive Merit Personnel Act of
195 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C. Official Code § 1-601.01 et seq.), is
196 amended as follows:
197 (a) Section 1204 (D.C. Official Code § 1-612.04) is amended as follows:
198 (1) Paragraph (4) is amended to read as follows:
199 “(4)(A) “Eligible employee” means a District government employee, including an
200 employee of an independent agency; provided, that for the purposes of using paid family leave or
201 paid medical leave, the term “eligible employee” means a District government employee,
202 including an employee of an independent agency, has worked for the District government for at
203 least 180 days, without a break in service, as of the date on which the paid family leave or paid
204 medical leave will be used.
205 “(B) The term “eligible employee” does not include:
206 “(i) A temporary employee appointed for less than 90 days; or
207 “(ii) An employee with intermittent employment.”.
208 (2) Paragraph (5) is amended as follows:
209 (A) Subparagraph (B) is amended by striking the semicolon at the end and
210 inserting the phrase “; or” in its place.
211 (B) Subparagraph (C) is amended to read as follows:
212 “(C) A spouse or domestic partner.”.
213 (C) Subparagraphs (D) and (E) are repealed.
214 (b) Section 1204a (D.C. Official Code § 1-612.04a) is amended as follows:
9

215 (1) Subsection (a)(1)(B) is amended by striking the phrase “8 workweeks” and
216 inserting the phrase “2 workweeks” in its place.
217 (2) A new subsection (c-1) is added to read as follows:
218 “(c-1)(1) To the extent practicable, an eligible employee shall, before using paid leave,
219 provide written notice to their personnel authority or agency of the need for the use of paid leave
220 and of the expected date or dates on which the employee intends to use paid leave.
221 “(2) If the employee plans to use paid leave on an intermittent basis, the written
222 notice shall, to the extent practicable, include a schedule of the expected hours during which the
223 employee intends to use paid leave.
224 “(3) The written notice shall include a reason for the use of paid leave, within the
225 parameters of the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996, approved August
226 21, 1996 (Pub. L. No. 104-191; 110 Stat. 1936).
227 “(4) If the use of paid leave is foreseeable, the written notice shall be provided at
228 least 10 days, or as early as possible, in advance of the use of the paid leave.
229 “(5) If the use of paid leave is unforeseeable, a notification, either oral or written,
230 shall be provided before the start of the work shift for which the paid leave is being used.
231 “(6) In the case of an emergency resulting in the use of paid leave without the
232 opportunity to provide prior notification, the eligible employee, or another individual on behalf
233 of the eligible employee, shall notify the Mayor, either orally or in writing, within 48 hours after
234 the emergency occurs.
235 “(7) If the agency determines that the use of paid leave is likely to interfere with
236 the operations of the agency, the agency and eligible employee shall engage in good-faith
237 negotiations on alternate dates or hours for the use of the paid leave. The agency may deny the
10

238 use of paid leave under this section if an employee does not agree to a reasonable request to
239 revise the dates or hours for the use of the paid leave.”.
240 (3) Subsection (d)(2) is amended to read as follows:
241 “(2) If a probationary employee voluntarily separates in violation of the 1-year
242 continuation of service agreement, the individual shall be indebted to the District government for
243 the salary paid during the leave period. Indebtedness incurred pursuant to this paragraph may be
244 treated in whole or in part as an erroneous payment pursuant to Title XXIX.”.
245 (4) A new subsection (d-1) is added to read as follows:
246 “(d-1)(1) An employee, other than an employee serving in a probationary capacity, using
247 paid parental, family, or medical leave shall be required to enter into a continuation of service
248 agreement. The continuation of service agreement shall require the employee to continue to
249 serve as a District employee for 12 weeks after the use of the paid parental, family, or medical
250 leave.
251 “(2) If the employee voluntarily separates in violation of the continuation of
252 service agreement, the individual shall be indebted to the District government for the salary paid
253 during the leave period. Indebtedness incurred pursuant to this paragraph may be treated in
254 whole or in part as an erroneous payment pursuant to Title XXIX.”.
255 SUBTITLE D. LOBBYIST LATE FILING PENALTY
256 Sec. 1031. Short title.
257 This subtitle may be cited as the “Lobbyist Late Filing Penalty Amendment Act of 2026”.
258 Sec. 1032. Section 232(c) of the Board of Ethics and Government Accountability
259 Establishment and Comprehensive Ethics Reform Amendment Act of 2011, effective April 27,
260 2012 (D.C. Law 19-124; D.C. Official Code § 1-1162.32(c)), is amended by striking the phrase
11

261 “up to 60 days (excluding Saturdays, Sundays, and holidays)” and inserting the phrase “up to 60

263 SUBTITLE E. MAYORAL TRANSITION
264 Sec. 1041. Short title.
265 This subtitle may be cited as the “Mayoral Transition Act of 2026”.
266 Sec. 1042. Definitions.
267 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term “Mayor-elect” means:
268 (a) The person who is certified as the successful candidate for the office of Mayor by the
269 Board of Elections following the 2026 general election held to determine the Mayor; and
270 (b) For the period of time between the general election and such certification, the person
271 announced and published by the Board of Elections as the unofficial winner of the general
272 election for Mayor, if such person was announced as the unofficial winner with a margin of
273 victory of at least 2% of the votes cast.
274 Sec. 1043. Purpose.
275 This subtitle authorizes the Mayor to take appropriate action to assure continuity in the
276 execution of the laws and in the conduct of the executive affairs of the District government. The
277 purpose of this subtitle is to provide for the orderly transfer of the executive duties and
278 responsibilities of the executive branch of the District government with the expiration of the term
279 of office of a Mayor and the assumption of those duties and responsibilities by a new Mayor.
280 Sec. 1044. Transition activities.
281 The Mayor, in the discharge of the Mayor’s duties pursuant to section 422 of the District
282 of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 790; D.C. Official Code §
283 1- 204.22), may:
12

284 (a) Make available to the Mayor-elect office space, furniture, furnishings, office
285 machines, and supplies, at whatever place or places within the District the Mayor shall designate,
286 at no cost to the Mayor-elect and his or her transition staff; and
287 (b) Make payments to the Mayor-elect to reimburse the Mayor-elect for payments made,
288 or to pay for costs incurred by the Mayor-elect, for the following:
289 (1) Compensation for the transition staff of the Mayor-elect at a rate that does not
290 exceed the rate prescribed pursuant to the District of Columbia Government Comprehensive
291 Merit Personnel Act of 1978, effective March 3,1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C. Official Code § 1-
292 601.01 et seq.); provided, that a person who holds a position in, or is considered to be an
293 employee of, the District government shall not receive compensation as a member of the Mayor-
294 elect’s transition staff under this subtitle;
295 (2) Reasonable expenses for the procurement by the Mayor-elect of services of
296 any expert or consultant, or organization thereof;
297 (3) Reasonable expenses incurred by the Mayor-elect for printing, binding, and
298 duplicating;
299 (4) Reasonable postage or mailing expenses incurred by the Mayor-elect
300 consistent with the Official Correspondence Regulations, effective April 7, 1977 (D.C. Law 1-
301 118; D.C. Official Code § 2-701 et seq.); and
302 (5) Reasonable expenses for communications equipment and services.
303 Sec. 1045. Limitation on amount.
304 The aggregate amount of payments made under section 1043 of this subtitle shall not
305 exceed $300,000.
306 Sec. 1046. Reporting.
13

307 (a) The Mayor-elect shall file a report, to be prepared with appropriate supporting
308 documentation, accounting for the expenditure of funds pursuant to this subtitle.
309 (b) The report prepared pursuant to subsection (a) of this section shall be submitted to the
310 Council by March 31, 2027.
311 SUBTITLE F. FAIR ELECTIONS PROGRAM
312 Sec. 1051. Short title.
313 This subtitle may be cited as the “Fair Elections Program Amendment Act of 2026”.
314 Sec. 1052. Section 332h(b)(2) of the Board of Ethics and Government Accountability
315 Establishment and Comprehensive Ethics Reform Amendment Act of 2011, effective May 5,
316 2018 (D.C. Law 22-94; D.C. Official Code § 1-1163.32h(b)(2)), is amended to read as follows:
317 “(2)(A) If a participating candidate’s certification is revoked pursuant to section
318 332c(c)(2), (3), (4) or, due to fraudulent activities, (5), the participating candidate shall be
319 personally liable for any expended base amount or matching payments.
320 “(B) Upon the application of a participating candidate, the Campaign
321 Finance Board may reduce in whole or part the participating candidate’s personal liability under
322 subparagraph (A) of this paragraph if the participating candidate terminates his or her candidacy
323 as described in section 332c(c)(4) for good cause not within the candidate’s control, such as
324 health reasons, or if the imposition of personal liability under subparagraph (A) of this paragraph
325 would result in financial hardship for the participating candidate; provided, that a candidate’s
326 termination of his or her candidacy due to the candidate’s low standing in polls, limited success
327 in raising funds for his or her candidacy, low expectation of electoral success, or similar electoral
328 reasons, or termination of his or her candidacy for political reasons, shall not be considered good
329 cause.”.

413 “TITLE V-A-i
414 “RENT PAYMENT REPORTING PROGRAM
415 “Sec. 530a. Rent payment reporting program.
416 “(a) The Mayor may establish and administer a rent payment reporting program under
417 which rental housing providers report a tenant’s rent payments, at the request of the tenant, to
418 one or more consumer credit bureaus.
18

419 “(b) The Mayor may require a rental housing provider that receives a grant, loan, tax
420 abatement, or other financial support (collectively, “financial assistance”) from the District to, as
421 a condition of the financial assistance:
422 “(1) Participate in the District’s rent payment reporting program;
423 “(2) Participate in a third-party rent payment reporting program approved by the
424 Mayor; or
425 “(3) Provide information on their tenants’ rent payment to consumer credit
426 bureaus.
427 “(c)(1) The Mayor may issue grants to rental housing providers who participate in the
428 District’s rent payment reporting program to pay the costs of set-up fees for reporting rent
429 payments to credit bureaus, annual fees for reporting rent payments to credit bureaus, technical
430 assistance for credit bureaus, and fees for pulling credit reports.
431 “(2) The requirements of the Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective
432 December 24, 2013 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), shall not apply to
433 grants issued under this subsection.
434 “(d) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
435 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
436 rules to implement this section.”.
437 SUBTITLE C. WORKFORCE HOUSING OPPORTUNITY TAX ABATEMENT
438 Sec. 2021. Short title.
439 This subtitle may be cited as the “Workforce Housing Opportunity Amendment Act of
440 2026”.
19

441 Sec. 2022. Chapter 8 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
442 follows:
443 (a) The table of contents is amended by adding a new section designation to read as
444 follows:
445 “47-860a. Workforce housing opportunity tax abatement.”
446 (b) A new section 47-860a is added to read as follows:
447 “Sec. 47-860a. Workforce opportunity tax abatement.
448 “(a) Real property tax imposed by § 47-811 on real property certified as eligible pursuant
449 to subsection (f) of this section shall be abated each year during the period set forth in subsection
450 (e) of this section, by the amount certified by the Mayor for that year; provided, that:
451 “(1) The real property is certified by the Mayor pursuant to subsection (b) of this
452 section;
453 “(2) The developer provides a fiscal analysis prepared by a third-party showing
454 the amount of abatement required for the feasibility of the project;
455 “(3) The real property is developed with at least 40 housing units;
456 “(4) For the duration of the period set forth in subsection (e) of this section, at
457 least 20% of the housing units developed or redeveloped on the real property are maintained as
458 affordable to households earning 80% or less of the median family income and at least 20% of
459 the housing units are maintained as affordable to households earning 80% to 100% of the median
460 family income;
461 “(5) The developer files a covenant in the land records of the District, binding on
462 the developer and all of its successors in interest with respect to the property, covenanting to
463 comply with the requirements of paragraph (5) of this subsection;
20

464 “(6) The developer enters into an agreement with the District that requires the
465 developer to, at a minimum, contract with certified business enterprises for at least 35% of the
466 contract dollar volume of the construction and operations of the project, in accordance with
467 section 2346 of the CBE Act (D.C. Official Code § 2-218.46);
468 “(7) The developer enters into a First Source Agreement for the construction,
469 development, and operations of the project; and
470 “(8) The developer enters into an agreement with the Mayor setting forth the
471 requirements of this subsection and such other terms and conditions as the Mayor considers
472 appropriate.
473 “(b) The Mayor may, through a competitive process, certify real property as eligible to
474 receive a tax abatement under this section; provided, that the total amount of the tax abatements
475 associated with real property certified by the Mayor pursuant to this subsection (the “maximum
476 fiscal year abatement amount”) shall not exceed:
477 “(1) $4 million in Fiscal Year 2029;
478 “(2) $5 million in Fiscal Year 2030;
479 “(3) $6 million in Fiscal Year 2031;
480 “(4) In Fiscal Year 2032 and each subsequent fiscal year, an amount equal to
481 105% of the prior year’s maximum fiscal year abatement amount.
482 “(c) The amount of the tax abatement certified by the Mayor for an individual abatement
483 shall be no greater than the amount needed for the feasibility of the project, as demonstrated by
484 an independent financial analysis, and shall not exceed the total amount of residential taxes due
485 for any year during the term of the abatement.
21

486 “(d)(1) A tax abatement certified by the Mayor under this section shall begin on the first
487 day of the tax year immediately following the tax year when the certificate of occupancy was
488 issued for the final housing unit counted toward satisfying the affordability requirement of
489 subsection (a)(5) of this section.
490 “(2) Notwithstanding paragraph (1) of this subsection, a tax abatement provided
491 for by this section shall not begin before October 1, 2028.
492 “(e) A tax abatement certified by the Mayor under this section shall continue until the end
493 of the 10th tax year after the tax year during which the requirement of subsection (d) is met;
494 provided, that the tax abatement provided for by this section may continue until the end of the
495 20th tax year after the tax year during which the requirement of subsection (d) is met if the
496 Mayor determines that the abatement is necessary for the feasibility of the project;
497 “(f)(1) The Mayor shall certify to the Office of Tax and Revenue a real property's
498 certification to receive the tax abatement provided by this section. The Mayor's certification shall
499 include:
500 “(A) A description of the real property certified to receive the tax
501 abatement by street address, square, suffix, and lot;
502 “(B) The date the tax abatement begins and ends under subsection (e) of
503 this section;
504 “(C) The annual amount of tax abatement allocated to the property
505 pursuant to subsection (b) of this section; and
506 “(D) A statement that the conditions specified in subsection (a) of this
507 section have been satisfied; and
22

508 “(E) Any other information that the Mayor considers necessary or
509 appropriate.
510 “(2) If at any time the Mayor determines that the real property has become
511 ineligible for the abatement provided by this section, the Mayor shall notify the Office of Tax
512 and Revenue and shall specify the date that the property became ineligible. The real property
513 shall be ineligible for the abatement on the first day of the tax year following the date when the
514 ineligibility occurred.
515 “(h) The tax abatement provided by this section shall be in addition to, not in lieu of, any
516 other tax relief or assistance from any other source.
517 “(i) For the purposes of this section, the term:
518 “(1) “CBE Act” means the Small and Certified Business Enterprise Development
519 and Assistance Act of 2005, effective October 20, 2005 (D.C. Law 16-33; D.C. Official Code §
520 2-218.01 et seq.).
521 “(2) “Certified business enterprise” means a business enterprise or joint venture
522 certified pursuant to the CBE Act.
523 “(3) “Developer” means the owner of housing units on real property eligible for a
524 tax abatement under this section.
525 “(4) “First Source Act” means the First Source Employment Agreement Act of
526 1984, effective June 29, 1984 (D.C. Law 5-93; D.C. Official Code § 2-219.01 et seq.).
527 “(5) “First Source Agreement” means an agreement with the District governing
528 certain obligations of the developer pursuant to section 4 of the First Source Act (D.C. Official
529 Code § 2-219.03), and Mayor’s Order 83-265, dated November 9, 1983, regarding job creation
530 and employment.
23

531 “(6) “Median family income” has the meaning set forth in section 101(5) of the
532 Inclusionary Zoning Implementation Amendment Act of 2006, effective September 23, 2017
533 (D.C. Law 16-275; D.C. Official Code § 6-1041.01(5)).
534 “(j) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
535 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
536 rules to implement this section.”.

594 “(ii) Is ground leased by the federal government to a private entity
595 after October 1, 2026, pursuant to a ground lease and development agreement between the
596 federal government and the private entity;
597 “(iii) Is developed pursuant to the ground lease and development
598 agreement with a project that has 200,000 square feet or more in gross floor area;
26

599 “(iv) Was not subject to tax under D.C. Official Code § 47-811 or

604 the District that:

621 determined by the Mayor; and
27

622 “(4) The owner or ground lessee demonstrates to the satisfaction of the Mayor:
623 “(A) That a tax abatement is necessary for the project to be financially
624 feasible;
625 “(B) The amount of the tax abatement necessary for the project to be
626 financially feasible; and
627 “(C) An ability to complete the project in a timely manner.
628 “(b) The tax abatement provided for by this section shall last for up to 20 consecutive real
629 property tax years beginning in the tax year commencing after the tax year in which the
630 certificate of occupancy was issued for the development on the property.
631 “(c) The number of years and annual amount of the tax abatement provided under this
632 section shall be the number and amount, as determined in the sole discretion of the Mayor,
633 subject to subsection (b) of this section, necessary for the project to be financially feasible and to
634 be timely initiated and continued to completion by the owner or ground lessee of the real
635 property.
636 “(d) If, 5 years after the District and the owner or ground lessee enter into the agreement
637 required by subsection (a)(2) of this section, the owner or ground lessee has not made substantial
638 progress in developing the project, as determined by the Mayor, the Mayor may terminate the
639 agreement and rescind the project’s eligibility for a tax abatement under this section.
640 “(e)(1) The Mayor shall certify to the Office of Tax and Revenue a real property’s
641 eligibility for the abatement provided by this section. The Mayor’s certification shall include:
642 “(A) A description of the real property by street address, square, suffix,
643 and lot;
644 “(B) The date the certificate of occupancy was issued;
28

645 “(C) The date the tax abatement begins and ends under subsections (b) and
646 (c) of this section;
647 “(D) A statement that the conditions specified in subsection (a) of this
648 section have been satisfied;
649 “(E) The amount of abatement allocated to the property pursuant to
650 subsection (c) of this section; and
651 “(F) Any other information that the Mayor considers necessary or
652 appropriate.
653 “(2) If at any time the Mayor determines that the real property has become
654 ineligible for the abatement provided by this section, the Mayor shall notify the Office of Tax
655 and Revenue and shall specify the date that the property became ineligible. The property shall be
656 ineligible for the abatement on the first day of the tax year following the date when the
657 ineligibility occurred.
658 “(f) For the purposes of this section, the term:
659 “(1) “CBE Act” means the Small and Certified Business Enterprise Development
660 and Assistance Act of 2005, effective October 20, 2005 (D.C. Law 16-33; D.C. Official Code §
661 2-218.01 et seq.).
662 “(2) “Certified business enterprise” means a business enterprise or joint venture

664 “(3) “Developer” means the owner of property eligible for a tax abatement under
665 this section.

29

668 “(5) “First Source Agreement” means an agreement with the District governing

670 Code § 2-219.03), and Mayor’s Order 83-265, dated November 9, 1983, regarding job creation
671 and employment.
672 “(6) “Special merit” means, with respect to a project under this section, providing
673 significant benefits to the District or to the community in which the project is located by virtue of

675 serving or regional retail; historical designation of the site on or building in which the project is

679 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
680 rules to implement this section.”.

770 Code § 2-219.03), and Mayor’s Order 83-265, dated November 9, 1983, regarding job creation
771 and employment.
772 “(7) “Joint development agreement” means a contract between WMATA and a
773 third party to sell or ground lease WMATA property for development.
774 “(8) “Special merit” means, with respect to a project under this section, providing
775 significant benefits to the District or to the community in which the project is located by virtue of
776 providing a significant number of housing units or a substantial square footage of neighborhood-
777 serving or regional retail; historical designation of the site on or building in which the project is
778 located; complexity of the development; or social or other benefits having a high priority in the
779 District or the community within the project is to be located.
34

780 (9) “WMATA” means the Washington Metropolitan Area Transit Authority.
781 “(g) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
782 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
783 rules to implement this section.”.
784 SUBTITLE F. FEDERAL PROPERTIES TAX FUND
785 Sec. 2051. Short title.
786 This subtitle may be cited as the “Federal Properties Tax Fund Act of 2026”.
787 Sec. 2052. Federal Property Tax Fund.
788 (a) There is established as a special fund the Federal Properties Tax Fund (“Fund”),
789 which shall be administered by the Mayor in accordance with subsections (c) and (d) of this
790 section.
791 (b) Revenue from the real property tax imposed by § 47-811 and the possessory interest
792 tax imposed by § 47-1005.01 on covered former federal properties shall be deposited in the
793 Fund.
794 “(c) Money in the Fund may be used to:
795 “(1) Implement and support infrastructure improvements, civic projects,
796 redevelopment, and property acquisition in the Central Washington Area, as such area is defined
797 in Volume 2 of the District’s 2021 Comprehensive Plan;
798 “(2) Pay debt service, including principal and interest, costs of issuance, and
799 credit enhancements, and any costs of defeasance on bonds issued to support development of a
800 covered former federal property; and
801 “(3) Pay the costs of tax abatements awarded pursuant to D.C. Official Code § 47-
802 861.05.
35

803 “(d) The money deposited into the Fund but not expended in a fiscal year shall not revert
804 to the unassigned fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia at the end of the
805 fiscal year, or at any other time.
806 “(e) For the purposes of this section, the term “covered former federal property” means:
807 “(A) A property that:
808 “(i) Is owned by the District;
809 “(ii) Was owned by the federal government immediately prior to
810 its ownership by the District;
811 “(iii) Was disposed by the federal government to the District after
812 October 1, 2026;
813 “(iv) Is ground leased to a private entity by the District pursuant to
814 a ground lease and development agreement;
815 “(v) Was not subject to tax under D.C. Official Code § 47-811 or §
816 47-1005.01 immediately prior to being ground leased by the District government; and
817 “(vi) Continues to be subject to the ground lease and development
818 agreement;
819 “(B) A property that:
820 “(i) Was owned by the District;
821 “(ii) Was owned by the federal government immediately prior to
822 its ownership by the District;
823 “(iii) Was disposed by the federal government to the District after
824 October 1, 2026;
36

825 “(iv) Was disposed of by the District pursuant to a sale and
826 development agreement between the District and a private entity;
827 “(v) Was not subject to tax under D.C. Official Code § 47-811 or §
828 47-1005.01 while owned by the District government or federal government; and
829 “(vi) Continues to be subject to the sale and development
830 agreement;
831 “(C) A property that:
832 “(i) Was owned by the federal government;
833 “(ii) Was disposed of by the federal government to a private entity
834 after October 1, 2026, pursuant to a sale and development agreement between the federal
835 government and the private entity;
836 “(iii) Was not subject to tax under D.C. Official Code § 47-811 or
837 § 47-1005.01 while owned by the federal government; and
838 “(iv) Continues to be subject to the sale and development
839 agreement; or
840 “(D) A property that:
841 “(i) Is owned by the federal government;
842 “(ii) Is ground leased by the federal government to a private entity
843 after October 1, 2026, pursuant to a ground lease and development agreement between the
844 federal government and the private entity;
845 “(iii) Was not subject to tax under D.C. Official Code § 47-811 or
846 § 47-1005.01 while owned by the federal government; and
37

847 “(iv) Continues to be subject to the ground lease and development
848 agreement.
849 “(f) The Mayor may, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative
850 Procedure Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.),
851 issue rules to implement this section.”.

1391 private gain is considered to control an entity if the organization:
1392 “(1) Owns a majority voting interest in the entity or the entity’s managing
1393 member; and
1394 “(2) Participates on a regular, continuous, and substantial basis in the day-to-day
1395 operation of, and management decision-making for, the affordable housing owned by or leased
1396 to the entity.”.

1486 TITLE III. PUBLIC SAFETY AND JUSTICE
1487 SUBTITLE A. PUBLIC SERVICES HOTEL OCCUPANCY FEE
1488 Sec. 3001. Short title.
1489 This subtitle may be cited as the “Public Services Hotel Occupancy Fee Amendment Act
1490 of 2026”.
1491 Sec. 3002. The Emergency and Non-Emergency Telephone Calling Systems Fund Act of
1492 2000, effective October 19, 2000 (D.C. Law 13-172; D.C. Official Code § 34-1801 et seq.), is
1493 amended by adding new sections 603a and 603b to read as follows:
1494 “Sec. 603a. Public services hotel occupancy fee.
1495 “(a) A fee, separate from, and in addition to, the taxes imposed by section 604 and D.C.
1496 Official Code §§ 47-2002(a)(2), 47-2002.02(1), 47-2002.03a, 2202(a)(2), 47-2202.02(1), and 47-
1497 2202.03a, is imposed on all hotels a fee of $.80 per hotel room per occupied night.
1498 “(b) The fee imposed by subsection (a) of this section shall be reported and remitted in
1499 the manner and form prescribed by the Chief Financial Officer under Chapter 20 of Title 47 of
67

1500 the District of Columbia Official Code and shall be subject to all collection, enforcement, and
1501 administrative provisions applicable to unpaid taxes or fees, as provided in Chapters 20, 41, 42,
1502 43, and 44 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code.
1503 “(c) The revenue received pursuant to the fee imposed by this section shall be deposited
1504 into the Public Services Telecommunications Fund established by section 603b.
1505 “(d) For the purposes of this section, the term:
1506 “(1) “Hotel” means a person that furnishes rooms, lodgings, or other
1507 accommodations to transients, including hotels, inns, tourist camps, tourist cabins, or any other
1508 place in which rooms, lodgings, or accommodations are regularly furnished to transients, for
1509 which the sale of or charges for are subject to taxation under D.C. Official Code § 47-2002(a)(2);
1510 and
1511 “(2) “Hotel room” means a room, suite of rooms, short term rental as defined in
1512 section 101(5) of the Short-Term Rental Regulation Act of 2018. effective April 25, 2019 (D.C.
1513 Law 22-307; D.C. Official Code § 30-201.01(5)), vacation rental as defined in section 101(6) of
1514 the Short-Term Rental Regulation Act of 2018. effective April 25, 2019 (D.C. Law 22-307; D.C.
1515 Official Code § 30-201.01(6)), or any other accommodation subject to the tax imposed by D.C.
1516 Official Code § 47-2002(a)(2).
1517 “Sec. 603b. Public Services Telecommunications Fund.
1518 “(a) There is established as a special fund the Public Services Telecommunications Fund
1519 (“Fund”), which shall be administered by the Mayor in accordance with this section.
1520 “(b) Revenue from the fee imposed by section 603a shall be deposited in the Fund.
1521 “(c) Money in the Fund may be used for the purposes described in section 603(c) and to
1522 pay for the costs of other public services.
68

1523 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined
1524 by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the unassigned
1525 fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal year-end
1526 close.”.

1633 SUBTITLE F. HOMELAND SECURITY COMMISSION DISSOLUTION
1634 Sec. 3051. Short title.
73

1635 This subtitle may be cited as the “Homeland Security Commission Dissolution
1636 Amendment Act of 2026”.
1637 Sec. 3052. Dissolution of the Homeland Security Commission.
1638 Title II of the Homeland Security, Risk Reduction, and Preparedness Amendment Act of
1639 2006, effective March 14, 2007 (D.C. Law 16-262; D.C. Code §§ 7-2271.01–7-2271.07), is
1640 repealed.
1641 Sec. 3053. Disposition of Homeland Security Commission records and information.
1642 All records and information of the Homeland Security Commission (“Commission”)
1643 shall, on October 1, 2026, become the records and information of the Homeland Security and
1644 Emergency Management Agency (“HSEMA”), and all such records and information obtained by
1645 the Commission pursuant to Title II of the Homeland Security, Risk Reduction, and
1646 Preparedness Amendment Act of 2006, effective March 14, 2007 (D.C. Law 16-262; D.C. Code
1647 §§ 7-2271.01–7-2271.07), shall be destroyed by HSEMA by September 30, 2027.
1648 Sec. 3054. Ongoing confidentiality.
1649 (a) Persons other than Homeland Security Commission (“Commission”) members who
1650 attended any Commission meeting which, pursuant to section 204 of the Homeland Security,
1651 Risk Reduction, and Preparedness Amendment Act of 2006, effective March 14, 2007 (D.C. Law
1652 16-262; D.C. Code §§ 7-2271.01–7-2271.04), was not open to the public, shall not disclose what
1653 occurred at the meeting to anyone who was not in attendance.
1654 (b) Commission members who attended meetings not open to the public shall not disclose
1655 what occurred with anyone who was not in attendance (except other Commission members).
1656 (c) Members of the Commission, persons who attended a Commission meeting, and
1657 persons who presented information to the Commission may not be required to disclose, in any
74

1658 administrative, civil, or criminal proceeding, information presented at or opinions formed as a
1659 result of a Commission meeting.
1660 (d) All information and records generated by the Commission, including statistical
1661 compilations and reports, and all information and records acquired by the Commission, are
1662 confidential and all such information and records in possession of the Homeland Security and
1663 Emergency Management Agency pursuant to section 3053 are confidential. Notwithstanding the
1664 foregoing, Commission information and records may be disclosed by the Homeland Security and
1665 Emergency Management Agency as necessary to carry out its duties and purposes. The
1666 information and records may be disclosed by the Homeland Security and Emergency
1667 Management Agency to another homeland security agency or a homeland security commission if
1668 the other agency or commission is governed by confidentiality provisions which afford the same
1669 or greater protections as those that were provided in Title II of the Homeland Security, Risk
1670 Reduction, and Preparedness Amendment Act of 2006, effective March 14, 2007 (D.C. Law 16-
1671 262; D.C. Code §§ 7-2271.01–7-2271.07).
1672 (e) Except as permitted by this section, information and records of the Commission shall
1673 not be disclosed voluntarily, pursuant to a subpoena, in response to a request for discovery in any
1674 adjudicative proceeding, or in response to a request made under made under Title II of the
1675 District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act, effective March 25, 1977 (D.C. Law 1-96;
1676 D.C. Official Code § 2-531 et seq.), nor shall it be introduced into evidence in any
1677 administrative, civil, or criminal proceeding.
1678 (f) Information and records that were presented to the Commission shall not be immune
1679 from subpoena or discovery, or prohibited from being introduced into evidence, solely because
75

1680 the information and records were made available to the Commission, if the information and
1681 records could have been obtained through other sources.

1765 SUBTITLE B. ADVANCED TECHNICAL CENTERS FUND

1768 2026”.
1769 Sec. 4012. The State Education Office Establishment Act of 2000, effective March 10,
1770 2015 (D.C. Law 20-196; D.C. Official Code § 38-2601 et seq.), is amended by adding a new
1771 section 7m to read as follows:
1772 “Sec 7m. Advanced Technical Center Fund.
1773 “(a) There is established as a special fund the Advanced Technical Centers Fund (“ATC
1774 Fund”), which shall be administered by the Office of the State Superintendent of Education in
1775 accordance with subsection (c) of this section.
1776 “(b) There shall be deposited into the ATC Fund funds paid to the District by private
1777 entities for the rental, use, or maintenance of space within an Advanced Technical Center
1778 facility.
1779 “(c) Money in the ATC Fund shall be used to pay costs incurred by the Office of the State
1780 Superintendent of Education in operating and administering Advanced Technical Centers.
1781 “(d) Any money remaining available in the ATC Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as
1782 determined by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the
1783 unassigned fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal
1784 year-end close.
85

1785 “(e) For the purposes of this subtitle, the term “Advanced Technical Center” shall have
1786 the same meaning as provided in section 7f-1(d)(1) of the State Education Office Establishment

2304 of 2026”.
2305 Sec. 6012. Chapter 18 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
2306 follows:
2307 (a) The table of contents is amended as follows:
2308 (1) The section designation for section 47-1806.12 is amended to read as follows:
2309 “47-1806.12. Tax on residents and non-residents — Credits — Alternative fuel
2310 infrastructure credit —Tax year 2014 through tax year 2026.”.
2311 (2) A new section designation is added to read as follows:
109

2312 “47-1806.12a. Tax on residents and non-residents — Credits — Alternative fuel
2313 infrastructure credit — Tax year 2027 through tax year 2036.”
2314 (b) The section heading of section 47-1806.12 is amended to read as follows:
2315 “§ 47-1806.12. Tax on residents and non-residents — Credits — Alternative fuel
2316 infrastructure credit —Tax year 2014 through tax year 2026.”.
2317 (c) A new section 47-1806.12a is added to read as follows:
2318 “§ 47-1806.12a. Tax on residents and non-residents — Credits — Alternative fuel
2319 infrastructure credit — Tax year 2027 through 2036.
2320 “(a) Beginning with the taxable year after December 31, 2026, through the taxable year
2321 ending December 31, 2036, there shall be allowed against the tax imposed on an eligible
2322 applicant by § 47-1806.03 a credit in the amount of 50% of the equipment and labor costs
2323 directly attributable to the purchase and installation by the taxpayer of alternative fuel storage
2324 and dispensing or charging equipment in a property that is the dwelling of the taxpayer and
2325 located in the District; provided, that the credit shall not exceed $1,000 per vehicle charging
2326 station.
2327 “(b) The equipment and labor costs for which a tax credit may be claimed under this
2328 section shall not include costs associated with the construction or purchase of any real property
2329 or structure.”.
2330 “(c) The credit claimed under this section in any one tax year may not exceed the
2331 taxpayer’s tax liability under § 47-1806.03 for that year.
2332 “(d) If the amount of the tax credit permitted under this section exceeds the tax otherwise
2333 due under § 47-1806.03, the amount of the credit not used may be carried forward for up to 2 tax
2334 years. The credit shall not be refundable.
110

2335 “(e) For the purposes of this section, the term:
2336 “(1) “Alternative fuel” means a fuel used to power a motor vehicle that consists of
2337 one or more of the following:
2338 “(A) Biodiesel, excluding kerosene;
2339 “(B) Electricity provided by a vehicle-charging station; or
2340 “(C) Hydrogen.
2341 “(2) “Eligible applicant” means a resident who is an owner or lessee of a qualified
2342 private residence.”.
2343 (c) Section 47-1807.10 is amended as follows:
2344 (1) Subsection (a) is amended by striking the date “December 31, 2026,” and
2345 inserting the date “December 31, 2036,” in its place.
2346 (2) Subsection (f)(1) is amended by striking the phrase “shall have the same
2347 meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12(f)(1)” and inserting the phrase “shall, through December
2348 31, 2026, have the same meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12(f)(1) and shall, after December
2349 31, 2026, have the same meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12a(e)(1)” in its place.
2350 (d) Section 47-1808.10 is amended as follows:
2351 (1) Subsection (a) is amended by striking the date “December 31, 2026,” and
2352 inserting the date “December 31, 2036” in its place.
2353 (2) Subsection (f)(1) is amended by striking the phrase “shall have the same
2354 meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12(f)(1)” and inserting the phrase “shall, through December
2355 31, 2026, have the same meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12(f)(1) and shall, after December
2356 31, 2026, have the same meaning as provided in § 47-1806.12a(e)(1)” in its place.

2393 the phrase “in section 107 of the Retail Electric Competition and Consumer Protection Act of

2397 1507a);” in its place.
2398 (c) Section 107 (D.C. Official Code § 34-1507) is amended as follows:
2399 (1) Subsection (a)(2) is amended to read as follows:
2400 “(2) This restriction shall not apply to lawful disclosures:
2401 “(A) For bill collection or credit rating reporting purposes;
113

2402 “(B) To a building owner about the energy consumption of a non-
2403 residential tenant of the building; or
2404 “(C) To comply with the reporting requirements of this act.”.
2405 (2) Subsection (b)(2) is amended to read as follows:
2406 “(2) This restriction shall not apply to lawful disclosures for bill collection, credit
2407 rating reporting purposes, or information disclosed in compliance with the reporting
2408 requirements of this act.”.
2409 (d) A new section 107a is added to read as follows:
2410 “Sec. 107a. Market participants: rates, termination of contracts, and other consumer
2411 protections.
2412 “(a) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, the supply and sale of electricity by a
2413 market participant to residential customers shall be regulated by the Commission as follows:
2414 “(1) A market participant shall only offer electricity supply to residential
2415 customers at a price that does not exceed the applicable price cap established by the Commission
2416 pursuant to subsection (b) of this section.
2417 “(2) Residential customers may terminate their supply contracts at any time and
2418 market participants shall not charge residential customers fees or penalties for early termination
2419 of service.
2420 “(3) A market participant shall be responsible for ensuring that its agents,
2421 contractors, marketers, or brokers comply with all legal requirements that apply to the supply and
2422 sale of electricity in the District, including the consumer protections in this section and section
2423 107, and associated regulations. A market participant shall be liable for any violation of these
2424 legal requirements committed by its agents, contractors, marketers, or brokers.
114

2425 “(b)(1) The Commission shall establish one or more price caps for electricity supplied by
2426 a market participant to residential customers. Except as provided in paragraphs (2) and (3) of
2427 this subsection, the price cap shall not exceed 110% of the price of the standard offer service.
2428 “(2) The Commission may establish a price cap that exceeds 110% of the price of
2429 the standard offer service if the electricity supply is sourced from a tier one renewable source or
2430 tier two renewable source, as those terms are defined in section 3 of the Renewable Energy
2431 Portfolio Standard Act of 2004, effective April 12, 2005 (D.C. Law 15-340; D.C. Official Code §
2432 34-1431), if a market participant demonstrates procurement of renewable energy or renewable
2433 energy credits, as described in section 5 of the Renewable Energy Portfolio Standard Act of
2434 2004, effective April 12, 2005 (D.C. Law 15-340; D.C. Official Code § 34–1433), in excess of
2435 the amount required by the renewable energy portfolio standard established pursuant to section 4
2436 of the Renewable Energy Portfolio Standard Act of 2004, effective April 12, 2005 (D.C. Law 15-
2437 340; D.C. Official Code § 34–1432).
2438 “(3)(A) The Commission may establish exemptions from a price cap, or establish
2439 a higher price cap, for specific market participants or types of electricity supply contracts if the
2440 Commission determines that doing so is in the public interest. In making this determination, the
2441 Commission may consider the following factors, along with any other factor the Commission
2442 deems relevant:
2443 “(i) Whether a proposed service is new or innovative;
2444 “(ii) The potential for the service to result in long-term savings for
2445 residential customers;
115

2446 “(iii) Any other energy-related benefits the service may provide,
2447 such as improvements in energy efficiency or the ability of residential customers to manage their
2448 energy costs; and
2449 “(iv) The potential costs or financial risks to customers.
2450 “(B) The Commission may modify or revoke an exemption or higher price
2451 cap established pursuant to this paragraph if the Commission determines that the exemption or
2452 higher price cap is no longer in the public interest or is otherwise no longer warranted.
2453 “(c) A contract that contains a price for electricity supply that exceeds an applicable price
2454 cap established pursuant to this section, including a contract entered into before the Commission
2455 established the price cap, shall be deemed null and void as against public policy; provided, that if
2456 the contract was entered into before the Commission established the price cap, the contract may
2457 remain in effect for up to 60 days and, if amended to be in compliance with the price cap within
2458 the 60-day period, shall not be considered null and void under this subsection.
2459 “(d)(1) The Commission shall require each market participant to share the standard
2460 contract terms for each contract to be offered to a residential customer on a Commission-
2461 approved comparison website before the contract is offered to the residential customer.
2462 “(2) The Commission shall determine which standard contract terms offered by a
2463 market participant shall be posted to the Commission-approved website.
2464 “(3) The Commission may designate its own website as the Commission-
2465 approved website, or another website that assists residential customers in comparing electricity
2466 supply contracts from different market participants.
2467 “(4) Market participants shall notify the Commission when standard contract
2468 terms for a new contract are posted to the Commission-approved website, when the standard
116

2469 contract terms for a contract posted to the Commission-approved website are modified, and when
2470 a contract is removed from the Commission-approved website. The Commission may establish
2471 rules regarding the form, content, and frequency at which such notifications must be provided to
2472 the Commission.
2473 “(e) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, the Commission shall establish
2474 additional reporting requirements for market participants supplying electricity to residential
2475 customers and the SOS administrator as follows:
2476 “(1) The Commission shall require market participants and the SOS administrator
2477 to report the following information:
2478 “(A) Name of the market participant;
2479 “(B) Number of distinct rates offered by each market participant and the
2480 price offered for each rate;
2481 “(C) Number of customers subscribed to each rate;
2482 “(D) Sales volume in kilowatt hours (kWh) for each rate;
2483 “(E) Number of customers in arrears and average arrears per customer,
2484 reported by rate;
2485 “(F) Number of customers who switched to and from the market
2486 participant during the reporting period for each rate; and
2487 “(G) Number of customers with different contract lengths for each rate.
2488 “(2)(A) The Commission shall determine which information provided by a market
2489 participant pursuant to paragraph (1) of this subsection shall be deemed confidential for the
2490 purposes of protecting proprietary business information.
117

2491 “(B) The Commission may direct market participants to submit both
2492 confidential and public versions of any required report, with confidential information redacted
2493 from the public version.
2494 “(C) The Commission shall make available to the public copies of market
2495 participant reports, with all confidential information redacted.
2496 “(D) The Commission shall share, upon request, copies of confidential
2497 versions of market participant reports with the Office of the People’s Counsel, the Office of the
2498 Attorney General, and the Department.
2499 “(3) Nothing in this subsection shall prohibit the use of confidential information
2500 to prepare statistics or other general data for publication when the statistics or other general data
2501 are published in a manner that prevents identification of particular persons or individual
2502 customer account information.
2503 “(4) Nothing in this subsection shall limit the authority of the Commission to
2504 establish additional reporting requirements, including the frequency for reporting of the
2505 information in paragraph (1) of this subsection, or to continue existing reporting requirements.
2506 “(f) The requirements in subsections (a), (b), and (c) of this section do not apply to
2507 electricity supplied by or through:
2508 “(1) The standard offer service;
2509 “(2) A municipal aggregation program under section 115 of the Retail Electric
2510 Competition and Consumer Protection Act of 1999, effective May 9, 2000 (D.C. Law 13-107;
2511 D.C. Official Code § 34-1515);
2512 “(3) A single-customer or multi-customer microgrid; or
118

2513 “(4) The District government, the federal government, or the agencies and
2514 instrumentalities of the District government or federal government.
2515 “(g) The Commission shall issue rules or orders to implement this section within 270
2516 days after the effective date of the Enhanced Consumer Protections in the Retail Energy Market
2517 Act of 2026.”.

2547 “Section 9a. Enhanced consumer protections in the residential retail market for natural

2549 “(a) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, the supply and sale of natural gas by a

2555 time and natural gas suppliers shall not charge residential customers fees or penalties for early
2556 termination of service.

2558 contractors, marketers, or brokers comply with all legal requirements that apply to the supply and
120

2559 sale of natural gas in the District, including the consumer protections in this section and section
2560 9, and associated regulations. A natural gas supplier shall be liable for any violation of these
2561 legal requirements committed by its agents, contractors, marketers, or brokers.

2563 by a natural gas supplier to residential customers. Except as provided in paragraph (2) of this
2564 subsection, the price cap shall not exceed 110% of the price of the gas company’s default
2565 service.
2566 “(2) The Commission may establish exemptions from the price cap, or establish a
2567 price cap that exceeds 110% of the price of the gas company’s default service, for specific
2568 natural gas suppliers or types of natural gas supply contracts if the Commission determines that

2865 “(b) The District of Columbia government shall not purchase a sport utility vehicle for
2866 government use unless the sport utility vehicle is:
2867 “(1) A security, emergency, rescue, snow removal, or armored vehicle; or
2868 “(2) A zero-emission vehicle that:
2869 “(1) Is capable of detecting objects or persons 3 feet or taller starting from
2870 at least 2 feet from the front, sides, and back of the vehicle;
2871 “(2) Is equipped with an automatic emergency braking system that is
2872 engaged when the system detects an imminent collision with a vehicle, object, or pedestrian in
2873 the path of the vehicle;
2874 “(3) Is equipped with a blind spot monitor that is engaged when an object
2875 or person is detected in the blind spot of the vehicle;
2876 “(4) Weighs no more than 5,500 pounds;
2877 “(5) Has a hood height of no more than 36 inches; and
2878 “(6) Has a front end with a downward slope of no less than 65 degrees.”.
