2988 SUBTITLE E. NORTHEAST HEIGHTS TIF
2989 Sec. 7041. Short title
2990 This subtitle may be cited as the “Northeast Heights Tax Increment Financing Act of
2991 2026”.
2992 Sec. 7042. Definitions.
2993 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
142

2994 (1) “Authorized Delegate” means the Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic
2995 Development, the Chief Financial Officer, the Treasurer, or any officer or employee of the
2996 executive office of the Mayor to whom the Mayor has delegated any of the Mayor’s functions
2997 under this subtitle pursuant to section 422(6) of the Home Rule Act.
2998 (2) “Available Real Property Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from
2999 the imposition of the tax provided for in Chapter 8 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia
3000 Official Code, inclusive of any penalties and interest charges, exclusive of the special tax
3001 provided for in section 481 of the Home Rule Act pledged to payment of general obligation
3002 indebtedness of the District.
3003 (3) “Available Sales Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from the
3004 imposition of the tax under Chapter 20 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code,
3005 including penalty and interest charges, exclusive of the portion thereof required to be deposited
3006 in the Washington Convention Center Fund established pursuant to section 208 of the
3007 Washington Convention Center Authority Act of 1994, effective September 28, 1994 (D.C. Law
3008 10-188; D.C. Official Code § 10-1202.08), and any amounts to be made available to the
3009 Washington Metropolitan Transit Authority pursuant to section 7101 of the Fiscal Year 2018
3010 Budget Support Act of 2017, effective December 13, 2017 (D.C. Law 22-0033; 64 DCMR
3011 7652), and section 2 of the Stable and Reliable Source of WMATA Revenues Act of 1982,
3012 effective April 30, 1982 (D.C. Law 4-103; D.C. Official Code 9-1111.15(b)(2)(A)).
3013 (4) “Available Tax Increment,” means the sum of the Available Sales Tax
3014 Revenues and Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Northeast Heights TIF
3015 Area in any fiscal year of the District minus the sum of Available Sales Tax Revenues and
143

3016 Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Northeast Heights TIF Area in the
3017 applicable base year.
3018 (5) “Bond Counsel” means a firm or firms of attorneys designated as bond
3019 counsel from time to time by the Mayor.
3020 (6) “Bonds” means the District of Columbia revenue bonds, notes, or other
3021 obligations (including refunding bonds, notes, and other obligations), in one or more series,
3022 authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle.
3023 (7) “Chairman” means the Chairman of the Council of the District of Columbia.
3024 (8) “Chief Financial Officer” means the Chief Financial Officer established by
3025 section 424(a)(1) of the Home Rule Act.
3026 (9) “Closing Documents” means all documents and agreements, other than
3027 Financing Documents, that may be necessary and appropriate to issue, sell, and deliver the
3028 Bonds, and includes agreements, certificates, letters, opinions, forms, receipts, and other similar
3029 instruments.
3030 (10) “Council” means the Council of the District of Columbia.
3031 (11) “Debt Service” means principal, premium, if any, and interest on the Bonds.
3032 (12) “Development Costs” has the same meaning as in section 2(13) of the Tax
3033 Increment Financing Authorization Act of 1998, effective September 11, 1998 (D.C. Law 12-
3034 143; D.C. Official Code § 2-1217.01(13)).
3035 (13) “Development Sponsor” means Standard Real Estate Development, a
3036 Washington, D.C. limited liability company qualified to do business in the District of Columbia,
3037 or any other entity that undertakes the development of the project with the approval of the
3038 Mayor.
144

3039 (14) “District” means the District of Columbia.
3040 (15) “Financing Documents” means the documents, other than Closing
3041 Documents, that relate to the financing or refinancing of transactions to be affected through the
3042 issuance, sale, and delivery of the Bonds, including any offering document, and any required
3043 supplements to any such documents.
3044 (16) “Home Rule Act” means the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
3045 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 774; D.C. Official Code § 1-201.01 et seq.).
3046 (17) “Project” means the financing, refinancing, or reimbursing of Development
3047 Costs incurred within the Northeast Heights TIF Area and adjoining parcels.
3048 (18) “Refunding Bonds” means the District of Columbia bonds, notes, or other
3049 obligations, in one or more series, authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle to refund the
3050 Bonds.
3051 (19) “TIF” means tax increment financing.
3052 Sec. 7043. Creation of the Northeast Heights TIF Fund.
3053 (a) There is established as a nonlapsing fund the Northeast Heights TIF Fund. The Chief
3054 Financial Officer shall deposit into the Northeast Heights TIF Fund the Available Tax Increment
3055 and any other taxes or fees specifically designated by law for deposit in the Northeast Heights
3056 TIF Fund.
3057 (b) The Mayor may pledge and create a security interest in the funds in the Northeast
3058 Heights TIF Fund, or any sub-account within the Northeast Heights TIF Fund, for the payment
3059 of debt service on the Bonds without further action by the Council as permitted by section 490(f)
3060 of the Home Rule Act. The payment of debt service shall be made in accordance with the
145

3061 provisions of the Financing Documents entered into by the District in connection with the
3062 issuance of the Bonds.
3063 (c) If, at the end of any fiscal year of the District, the balance of cash and investments in
3064 the Northeast Heights TIF Fund exceeds the amount of debt service (including prepayment of
3065 principal and interest), reserves on any Bonds, and any approved Bond-related administrative
3066 expenses during the upcoming fiscal year, 50% of the excess shall be retained in the Northeast
3067 Heights TIF Fund to prepay the principal of the Bonds or for future reserves or administrative
3068 expenses on the Bonds and the remaining 50% of the excess shall be transferred to the
3069 unrestricted balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia.
3070 Sec. 7044. Creation of the Northeast Heights TIF Area.
3071 (a) There is created a TIF area designated as the Northeast Heights TIF Area, which shall
3072 consist of Square 5051N, Lot 19, Square 5051, Lots 28, 29, 811, and Square 5044, Lot 814 as
3073 shown on the tax rolls of the District as maintained by the Office of Tax and Revenue.
3074 (b) As provided in section 7043, the Available Tax Increment from the Northeast Heights
3075 TIF Area shall be deposited in the Northeast Heights TIF Fund and may be used for the purposes
3076 set forth in section 7045.
3077 (c)(1) The base year for determination of Available Sales Tax Revenues shall be the tax
3078 year of the District preceding the year in which act becomes effective.
3079 (2) The base year for determination of Available Real Property Tax Revenues
3080 shall be the tax year of the District preceding the year in which act becomes effective and the
3081 initial assessed value to be used in making the determination of Available Real Property Tax
3082 Revenues shall be the assessed value of each lot of taxable real property in the Northeast Heights
3083 TIF Area for the tax year preceding the tax year in which this subtitle becomes effective.
146

3084 (d) The Northeast Heights Area shall terminate on the earliest of:
3085 (1) December 31, 2056;
3086 (2) The date on which the Bonds are paid in full or are defeased and are no longer
3087 outstanding; and
3088 (3) Five years after the effective date of this subtitle if no Bonds are issued.
3089 Sec. 7045. Bond authorization.
3090 (a) The Council approves and authorizes the issuance of one or more series of Bonds in
3091 an aggregate principal amount not to exceed $47 million to fund the project. The Bonds, which
3092 may be issued from time to time, in one or more series, shall be tax-exempt or taxable as the
3093 Mayor shall determine and shall be payable and secured as provided in section 7046.
3094 (b) The proceeds of the Bonds shall be used to pay Development Costs of the Project,
3095 financing costs incurred by the District and to fund capitalized interest and required reserves.
3096 (c) The Mayor may pay from the proceeds of the Bonds the financing costs and expenses
3097 of issuing and delivering the Bonds, including underwriting, legal, accounting, financial
3098 advisory, credit enhancement, marketing, sale, and printing costs and expenses.
3099 Sec. 7046. Payment and security.
3100 (a) Except as may be otherwise provided in this subtitle, the principal of, premium, if
3101 any, and interest on, the Bonds, and the payment of ongoing administrative expenses related to
3102 the Bond financing shall be payable solely from proceeds received from the sale of the Bonds,
3103 income realized from the temporary investment of those proceeds, Available Tax Increment and
3104 other taxes and fees specifically designated by law for deposit into the Northeast Heights TIF
3105 Fund, income realized from the temporary investment of those receipts and revenues prior to
3106 payment to the Bond owners, and other funds that, as provided in the Financing Documents, may
147

3107 be made available to the District for payment of the Bonds from sources other than the District,
3108 all as provided for in the Financing Documents.
3109 (b) Payment of the Bonds shall be secured as provided in the Financing Documents and
3110 by an assignment by the District for the benefit of the Bond owners of certain of its rights under
3111 the Financing Documents and Closing Documents to the trustee for the Bonds pursuant to the
3112 Financing Documents.
3113 (c) The trustee or paying agent is authorized to deposit, invest, and disburse the proceeds
3114 received from the sale of the Bonds pursuant to the Financing Documents.
3115 Sec. 7047. Bond details.
3116 (a) The Mayor is authorized to take any action reasonably necessary or appropriate in
3117 accordance with this subtitle in connection with the preparation, execution, issuance, sale,
3118 delivery, security for, and payment of the Bonds of each class and series, including
3119 determinations of:
3120 (1) The final form, content, designation, and terms of the Bonds, including a
3121 determination that the Bonds may be issued in certificated or book-entry form;
3122 (2) The principal amount of the Bonds to be issued and denominations of the
3123 Bonds;
3124 (3) The rate or rates of interest or the method for determining the rate or rates of
3125 interest on the Bonds;
3126 (4) The date or dates of issuance, sale, and delivery of, and the payment of interest
3127 on, the Bonds, and the maturity date or dates of the Bonds;
148

3128 (5) The terms under which the Bonds may be paid, optionally or mandatorily
3129 redeemed, accelerated, tendered, called, or put for redemption, repurchase, or remarketing before
3130 their respective stated maturities;
3131 (6) Provisions for the registration, transfer, and exchange of the Bonds and the
3132 replacement of mutilated, lost, stolen, or destroyed Bonds;
3133 (7) The creation of any reserve fund, sinking fund, or other fund with respect to
3134 the Bonds;
3135 (8) The time and place of payment of the Bonds;
3136 (9) Procedures for monitoring the use of the proceeds received from the sale of
3137 the Bonds to ensure that the proceeds are properly applied and used to accomplish the purposes
3138 of the Home Rule Act and this subtitle;
3139 (10) Actions necessary to qualify the Bonds under blue sky laws of any
3140 jurisdiction where the Bonds are marketed; and
3141 (11) The terms and types of any credit enhancement under which the Bonds may
3142 be secured.
3143 (b) The Bonds shall contain a legend which shall provide that the Bonds are special
3144 obligations of the District, are without recourse to the District, are not a pledge of, and do not
3145 involve, the faith and credit or the taxing power of the District (other than the Available Tax
3146 Increment, and any other taxes and fees deposited in the Northeast Heights Phase 2 TIF Fund),
3147 do not constitute a debt of the District, and do not constitute lending of the public credit for
3148 private undertakings as prohibited in section 602(a)(2) of the Home Rule Act.
149

3149 (c) The Bonds shall be executed in the name of the District and on its behalf by the
3150 manual or facsimile signature of the Mayor, and attested by the Secretary of the District of
3151 Columbia by the Secretary’s manual or facsimile signature.
3152 (d) The official seal of the District, or a facsimile of it, shall be impressed, printed, or
3153 otherwise reproduced on the Bonds.
3154 (e) The Bonds of any series may be issued in accordance with the terms of a trust
3155 instrument to be entered into by the District and a trustee or paying agent to be selected by the
3156 Mayor, and may be subject to the terms of one or more agreements entered into by the Mayor
3157 pursuant to section 490(a)(4) of the Home Rule Act.
3158 (f) The Bonds may be issued at any time or from time to time in one or more issues and
3159 in one or more series.
3160 (g) The Bonds are declared to be issued for essential public and governmental purposes.
3161 The Bonds, the interest thereon, and the income therefrom, and all funds pledged or available to
3162 pay or secure the payment of the Bonds, shall at all times be exempt from taxation by the
3163 District, except for estate, inheritance, and gift taxes.
3164 (h) The District pledges, covenants, and agrees with the holders of the Bonds that, subject
3165 to the provisions of the Financing Documents, the District will not limit or alter the revenues
3166 pledged to secure the Bonds or the basis on which such revenues are collected or allocated, will
3167 not impair the contractual obligations of the District to fulfill the terms of any agreement made
3168 with the holders of the Bonds, will not in any way impair the rights or remedies of the holders of
3169 the Bonds, and will not modify, in any way, the exemptions from taxation provided for in this
3170 subtitle, until the Bonds, together with interest thereon, and all costs and expenses in connection
3171 with any suit, action, or proceeding by or on behalf of the holders of the Bonds, are fully met and
150

3172 discharged. This pledge and agreement for the District may be included as part of the contract
3173 with the holders of the Bonds. This subsection constitutes a contract between the District and the
3174 holders of the Bonds. To the extent that any acts or resolutions of the Council may be in conflict
3175 with this subtitle, this subtitle shall be controlling.
3176 (i) Consistent with section 490(a)(4)(B) of the Home Rule Act (D.C. Official Code § 1-
3177 204.90(a)(4)(B)) and notwithstanding Article 9 of Subtitle I of Title 28of the District of
3178 Columbia Official Code:
3179 (1) A pledge made and security interest created in respect of the Bonds or
3180 pursuant to any related Financing Document shall be valid, binding, and perfected from the time
3181 the security interest is created, with or without physical delivery of any funds or any property
3182 and with or without any further action;
3183 (2) The lien of the pledge shall be valid, binding, and perfected as against all
3184 parties having any claim of any kind in tort, contract, or otherwise against the District, whether
3185 or not such party has notice; and
3186 (3) The security interest shall be valid, binding, and perfected whether or not any
3187 statement, document, or instrument relating to the security interest is recorded or filed.
3188 Sec.7048. Issuance of the Bonds.
3189 (a) The Bonds of any series may be sold at negotiated or competitive sale at, above, or
3190 below par, to one or more persons or entities, and upon terms that the Mayor considers to be in
3191 the best interests of the District.
3192 (b) The Mayor or an Authorized Delegate may execute, in connection with each sale of
3193 the Bonds, offering documents on behalf of the District, may deem final any such offering
3194 document on behalf of the District for purposes of compliance with federal laws and regulations
151

3195 governing such matters, and may authorize the distribution of the documents in connection with
3196 the Bonds.
3197 (c) The Mayor is authorized to deliver executed and sealed Bonds, on behalf of the
3198 District, for authentication, and, after the Bonds have been authenticated, to deliver the Bonds to
3199 the original purchasers of the Bonds upon payment of the purchase price.
3200 (d) The Bonds shall not be issued until the Mayor receives an approving opinion from
3201 Bond Counsel as to the validity of the Bonds of such series and, if the interest on the Bonds is
3202 expected to be exempt from federal income taxation, the treatment of the interest on the Bonds
3203 for purposes of federal income taxation.
3204 (e) The Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective April 8, 2011 (D.C. Law
3205 18-371; D.C. Official Code § 2-351.01 et seq.), and subchapter III-A of Chapter 3 of Title 47 of
3206 the District of Columbia Official Code shall not apply to any contract the Mayor may from time
3207 to time enter into, or the Mayor may determine to be necessary or appropriate, for the purposes
3208 of this subtitle.
3209 Sec. 7049. Financing and Closing Documents.
3210 (a) The Mayor is authorized to prescribe the final form and content of all Financing
3211 Documents and all Closing Documents to which the District is a party that may be necessary or
3212 appropriate to issue, sell, and deliver the Bonds.
3213 (b) The Mayor is authorized to execute, in the name of the District and on its behalf, the
3214 Financing Documents and any Closing Documents to which the District is a party by the
3215 Mayor’s manual or facsimile signature.
152

3216 (c) If required, the official seal of the District, or a facsimile of it, shall be impressed,
3217 printed, or otherwise reproduced on the Bonds, the other Financing Documents, and the Closing
3218 Documents to which the District is a party.
3219 (d) The Mayor’s execution and delivery of the Financing Documents and the Closing
3220 Documents to which the District is a party shall constitute conclusive evidence of the Mayor’s
3221 approval, on behalf of the District, of the final form and content of the executed Financing
3222 Documents and the executed Closing Documents.
3223 (e) The Mayor is authorized to deliver the executed and sealed Financing Documents and
3224 Closing Documents, on behalf of the District, prior to or simultaneously with the issuance, sale,
3225 and delivery of the Bonds, and to ensure the due performance of the obligations of the District
3226 contained in the executed, sealed, and delivered Financing Documents and Closing Documents.
3227 Sec.7050. Limited liability.
3228 (a) The Bonds shall be special obligations of the District. The Bonds shall be without
3229 recourse to the District. The Bonds shall not be general obligations of the District, shall not be a
3230 pledge of, or involve, the faith and credit or the taxing power of the District (other than the
3231 Available Tax Increment,, and any other taxes or fees allocated to the Northeast Heights TIF
3232 Fund), shall not constitute a debt of the District, and shall not constitute lending of the public
3233 credit for private undertakings as prohibited in section 602(a)(2) of the Home Rule Act.
3234 (b) The Bonds shall not give rise to any pecuniary liability of the District and the District
3235 shall have no obligation with respect to the purchase of the Bonds.
3236 (c) No person, including any Bond owner, shall have any claims against the District or
3237 any of its elected or appointed officials, officers, employees, or agents for monetary damages
3238 suffered as a result of the failure of the District to perform any covenant, undertaking, or
153

3239 obligation under this subtitle, the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents,
3240 or as a result of the incorrectness of any representation in or omission from the Financing
3241 Documents or the Closing Documents, unless the District or its elected or appointed officials,
3242 officers, employees, or agents have acted in a willful and fraudulent manner.
3243 Sec. 7051. District officials.
3244 (a) Except as otherwise provided in section 7050(c), the elected or appointed officials,
3245 officers, employees, or agents of the District shall not be liable personally for the payment of the
3246 Bonds or be subject to any personal liability by reason of the issuance of the Bonds, or for any
3247 representations, warranties, covenants, obligations, or agreements of the District contained in this
3248 subtitle, the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents.
3249 (b) The signature, countersignature, facsimile signature, or facsimile countersignature of
3250 any official appearing on the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents shall
3251 be valid and sufficient for all purposes notwithstanding the fact that the individual signatory
3252 ceases to hold that office before delivery of the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing
3253 Documents.
3254 Sec. 7052. Maintenance of documents.
3255 Copies of the specimen Bonds and of the final Financing Documents and Closing
3256 Documents shall be filed in the Office of the Secretary of the District of Columbia.
3257 Sec. 7053. Information reporting.
3258 Within 3 days after the Mayor’s receipt of the transcript of proceedings relating to the
3259 issuance of the Bonds, the Mayor shall transmit a copy of the transcript to the Secretary to the
3260 Council.
3261 SUBTITLE F. BRYANT STREET PHASE 2 TIF
154

3262 Sec. 7061. Short title
3263 This subtitle may be cited as the “Bryant Street Phase 2 Tax Increment Financing Act of
3264 2026”.
3265 Sec. 7062. Definitions.
3266 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
3267 (1) “Authorized Delegate” means the Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic
3268 Development, the Chief Financial Officer, the Treasurer, or any officer or employee of the
3269 executive office of the Mayor to whom the Mayor has delegated any of the Mayor’s functions
3270 under this subtitle pursuant to section 422(6) of the Home Rule Act.
3271 (2) “Available Real Property Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from
3272 the imposition of the tax provided for in Chapter 8 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia
3273 Official Code, inclusive of any penalties and interest charges, exclusive of the special tax
3274 provided for in section 481 of the Home Rule Act pledged to payment of general obligation
3275 indebtedness of the District.
3276 (3) “Available Sales Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from the
3277 imposition of the tax under Chapter 20 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code,
3278 including penalty and interest charges, exclusive of the portion thereof required to be deposited
3279 in the Washington Convention Center Fund established pursuant to section 208 of the
3280 Washington Convention Center Authority Act of 1994, effective September 28, 1994 (D.C. Law
3281 10-188; D.C. Official Code § 10-1202.08), and any amounts to be made available to the
3282 Washington Metropolitan Transit Authority pursuant to section 7101 of the Fiscal Year 2018
3283 Budget Support Act of 2017, effective December 13, 2017 (D.C. Law 22-0033; 64 DCMR
155

3284 7652), and section 2 of the Stable and Reliable Source of WMATA Revenues Act of 1982,
3285 effective April 30, 1982 (D.C. Law 4-103; D.C. Official Code 9-1111.15(b)(2)(A)).
3286 (4) “Available Tax Increment” means the sum of the Available Sales Tax
3287 Revenues and Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF
3288 Area in any fiscal year of the District minus the sum of Available Sales Tax Revenues and
3289 Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Area in the
3290 applicable base year.
3291 (5) “Bond Counsel” means a firm or firms of attorneys designated as bond
3292 counsel from time to time by the Chief Financial Officer.
3293 (6) “Bonds” means the District of Columbia revenue bonds, notes, or other
3294 obligations (including refunding bonds, notes, and other obligations), in one or more series,
3295 authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle.
3296 (7) “Chairman” means the Chairman of the Council of the District of Columbia.
3297 (8) “Chief Financial Officer” means the Chief Financial Officer established by
3298 section 424(a)(1) of the Home Rule Act.
3299 (9) “Closing Documents” means all documents and agreements, other than
3300 Financing Documents, that may be necessary and appropriate to issue, sell, and deliver the
3301 Bonds, and includes agreements, certificates, letters, opinions, forms, receipts, and other similar
3302 instruments.
3303 (10) “Council” means the Council of the District of Columbia.
3304 (11) “Debt Service” means principal, premium, if any, and interest on the Bonds.
156

3305 (12) “Development Costs” has the same meaning as in section 2(13) of the Tax
3306 Increment Financing Authorization Act of 1998, effective September 11, 1998 (D.C. Law 12-
3307 143; D.C. Official Code § 2-1217.01(13)).
3308 (13) “Development Sponsor” means MBR Venture Phase 2, LLC, a Delaware
3309 limited liability company qualified to do business in the District of Columbia, or any other entity
3310 that undertakes the development of the project with the approval of the Mayor.
3311 (14) “District” means the District of Columbia.
3312 (15) “Financing Documents” means the documents, other than Closing
3313 Documents, that relate to the financing or refinancing of transactions to be affected through the
3314 issuance, sale, and delivery of the Bonds, including any offering document, and any required
3315 supplements to any such documents.
3316 (16) “Home Rule Act” means the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
3317 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 774; D.C. Official Code § 1-201.01 et seq.).
3318 (17) “Project” means the financing, refinancing, or reimbursing of Development
3319 Costs incurred within the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Area and adjoining parcels.
3320 (18) “Refunding Bonds” means the District of Columbia bonds, notes, or other
3321 obligations, in one or more series, authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle to refund the
3322 Bonds.
3323 (19) “TIF” means tax increment financing.
3324 Sec. 7063. Creation of the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Fund.
3325 (a) There is established as a nonlapsing fund the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Fund. The
3326 Chief Financial Officer shall deposit into the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Fund the Available Tax
157

3327 Increment and any other taxes or fees specifically designated by law for deposit in the Bryant
3328 Street Phase 2 TIF Fund.
3329 (b) The Mayor may pledge and create a security interest in the funds in the Bryant Street
3330 Phase 2 TIF Fund, or any sub-account within the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Fund, for the
3331 payment of debt service on the Bonds without further action by the Council as permitted by
3332 section 490(f) of the Home Rule Act. The payment of debt service shall be made in accordance
3333 with the provisions of the Financing Documents entered into by the District in connection with
3334 the issuance of the Bonds.
3335 (c) If, at the end of any fiscal year of the District, the balance of cash and investments in
3336 the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF Fund exceeds the amount of debt service (including prepayment of
3337 principal and interest), reserves on any Bonds, and any approved Bond-related administrative
3338 expenses during the upcoming fiscal year, 50% of the excess shall be retained in the Bryant
3339 Street Phase 2 TIF Fund to prepay the principal of the Bonds or for future reserves or
3340 administrative expenses on the Bonds and the remaining 50% of the excess shall be transferred
3341 to the unrestricted balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia.

3451 otherwise reproduced on the Bonds.
3452 (e) The Bonds of any series may be issued in accordance with the terms of a trust
3453 instrument to be entered into by the District and a trustee or paying agent to be selected by the
3454 Mayor, and may be subject to the terms of one or more agreements entered into by the Mayor
3455 pursuant to section 490(a)(4) of the Home Rule Act.
3456 (f) The Bonds may be issued at any time or from time to time in one or more issues and
3457 in one or more series.
3458 (g) The Bonds are declared to be issued for essential public and governmental purposes.
3459 The Bonds, the interest thereon, and the income therefrom, and all funds pledged or available to
3460 pay or secure the payment of the Bonds, shall at all times be exempt from taxation by the
3461 District, except for estate, inheritance, and gift taxes.
163

3462 (h) The District pledges, covenants, and agrees with the holders of the Bonds that, subject
3463 to the provisions of the Financing Documents, the District will not limit or alter the revenues
3464 pledged to secure the Bonds or the basis on which such revenues are collected or allocated, will
3465 not impair the contractual obligations of the District to fulfill the terms of any agreement made
3466 with the holders of the Bonds, will not in any way impair the rights or remedies of the holders of
3467 the Bonds, and will not modify, in any way, the exemptions from taxation provided for in this
3468 subtitle, until the Bonds, together with interest thereon, and all costs and expenses in connection
3469 with any suit, action, or proceeding by or on behalf of the holders of the Bonds, are fully met and
3470 discharged. This pledge and agreement for the District may be included as part of the contract
3471 with the holders of the Bonds. This subsection constitutes a contract between the District and the
3472 holders of the Bonds. To the extent that any acts or resolutions of the Council may be in conflict
3473 with this subtitle, this subtitle shall be controlling.
3474 (i) Consistent with section 490(a)(4)(B) of the Home Rule Act (D.C. Official Code § 1-
3475 204.90) and notwithstanding Article 9 of Subtitle I of Title 28 of the District of Columbia
3476 Official Code:
3477 (1) A pledge made and security interest created in respect of the Bonds or
3478 pursuant to any related Financing Document shall be valid, binding, and perfected from the time
3479 the security interest is created, with or without physical delivery of any funds or any property
3480 and with or without any further action;
3481 (2) The lien of the pledge shall be valid, binding, and perfected as against all
3482 parties having any claim of any kind in tort, contract, or otherwise against the District, whether
3483 or not such party has notice; and
164

3484 (3) The security interest shall be valid, binding, and perfected whether or not any
3485 statement, document, or instrument relating to the security interest is recorded or filed.
3486 Sec. 7068. Issuance of the Bonds.
3487 (a) The Bonds of any series may be sold at negotiated or competitive sale at, above, or
3488 below par, to one or more persons or entities, and upon terms that the Mayor considers to be in
3489 the best interests of the District.
3490 (b) The Mayor or an Authorized Delegate may execute, in connection with each sale of
3491 the Bonds, offering documents on behalf of the District, may deem final any such offering
3492 document on behalf of the District for purposes of compliance with federal laws and regulations
3493 governing such matters, and may authorize the distribution of the documents in connection with
3494 the Bonds.
3495 (c) The Mayor is authorized to deliver executed and sealed Bonds, on behalf of the
3496 District, for authentication, and, after the Bonds have been authenticated, to deliver the Bonds to
3497 the original purchasers of the Bonds upon payment of the purchase price.
3498 (d) The Bonds shall not be issued until the Mayor receives an approving opinion from
3499 Bond Counsel as to the validity of the Bonds of such series and, if the interest on the Bonds is
3500 expected to be exempt from federal income taxation, the treatment of the interest on the Bonds
3501 for purposes of federal income taxation.
3502 (e) The Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective April 8, 2011 (D.C. Law
3503 18-371; D.C. Official Code § 2-351.01 et seq.), and subchapter III-A of Chapter 3 of Title 47 of
3504 the District of Columbia Official Code shall not apply to any contract the Mayor may from time
3505 to time enter into, or the Mayor may determine to be necessary or appropriate, for the purposes
3506 of this subtitle.
165

3507 Sec. 7069. Financing and Closing Documents.
3508 (a) The Mayor is authorized to prescribe the final form and content of all Financing
3509 Documents and all Closing Documents to which the District is a party that may be necessary or
3510 appropriate to issue, sell, and deliver the Bonds.
3511 (b) The Mayor is authorized to execute, in the name of the District and on its behalf, the
3512 Financing Documents and any Closing Documents to which the District is a party by the
3513 Mayor’s manual or facsimile signature.
3514 (c) If required, the official seal of the District, or a facsimile of it, shall be impressed,
3515 printed, or otherwise reproduced on the Bonds, the other Financing Documents, and the Closing
3516 Documents to which the District is a party.
3517 (d) The Mayor’s execution and delivery of the Financing Documents and the Closing
3518 Documents to which the District is a party shall constitute conclusive evidence of the Mayor’s
3519 approval, on behalf of the District, of the final form and content of the executed Financing
3520 Documents and the executed Closing Documents.
3521 (e) The Mayor is authorized to deliver the executed and sealed Financing Documents and
3522 Closing Documents, on behalf of the District, prior to or simultaneously with the issuance, sale,
3523 and delivery of the Bonds, and to ensure the due performance of the obligations of the District
3524 contained in the executed, sealed, and delivered Financing Documents and Closing Documents.
3525 Sec.7070. Limited liability.
3526 (a) The Bonds shall be special obligations of the District. The Bonds shall be without
3527 recourse to the District. The Bonds shall not be general obligations of the District, shall not be a
3528 pledge of, or involve, the faith and credit or the taxing power of the District (other than the
3529 Available Tax Increment and any other taxes or fees allocated to the Bryant Street Phase 2 TIF
166

3530 Fund), shall not constitute a debt of the District, and shall not constitute lending of the public
3531 credit for private undertakings as prohibited in section 602(a)(2) of the Home Rule Act.
3532 (b) The Bonds shall not give rise to any pecuniary liability of the District and the District
3533 shall have no obligation with respect to the purchase of the Bonds.
3534 (c) No person, including any Bond owner, shall have any claims against the District or
3535 any of its elected or appointed officials, officers, employees, or agents for monetary damages
3536 suffered as a result of the failure of the District to perform any covenant, undertaking, or
3537 obligation under this subtitle, the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents,
3538 or as a result of the incorrectness of any representation in or omission from the Financing
3539 Documents or the Closing Documents, unless the District or its elected or appointed officials,
3540 officers, employees, or agents have acted in a willful and fraudulent manner.
3541 Sec. 7071. District officials.
3542 (a) Except as otherwise provided in section 7070(c), the elected or appointed officials,
3543 officers, employees, or agents of the District shall not be liable personally for the payment of the
3544 Bonds or be subject to any personal liability by reason of the issuance of the Bonds, or for any
3545 representations, warranties, covenants, obligations, or agreements of the District contained in this
3546 subtitle, the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents.
3547 (b) The signature, countersignature, facsimile signature, or facsimile countersignature of
3548 any official appearing on the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing Documents shall
3549 be valid and sufficient for all purposes notwithstanding the fact that the individual signatory
3550 ceases to hold that office before delivery of the Bonds, the Financing Documents, or the Closing
3551 Documents.
3552 Sec. 7072. Maintenance of documents.
167

3553 Copies of the specimen Bonds and of the final Financing Documents and Closing
3554 Documents shall be filed in the Office of the Secretary of the District of Columbia.
3555 Sec. 7073. Information reporting.
3556 Within 3 days after the Mayor’s receipt of the transcript of proceedings relating to the
3557 issuance of the Bonds, the Mayor shall transmit a copy of the transcript to the Secretary to the
3558 Council.
3559 SUBTITLE G. REEVES TIF
3560 Sec. 7081. Short title.
3561 This subtitle may be cited as the “Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center Tax Increment
3562 Financing Act of 2026”.
3563 Sec. 7082. Definitions.
3564 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
3565 (1) “Authorized Delegate” means the Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic
3566 Development, the Chief Financial Officer, the Treasurer, or any officer or employee of the
3567 executive office of the Mayor to whom the Mayor has delegated any of the Mayor’s functions
3568 under this subtitle pursuant to section 422(6) of the Home Rule Act.
3569 (2) “Available Real Property Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from
3570 the imposition of the tax provided for in Chapter 8 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia
3571 Official Code, inclusive of any penalties and interest charges, exclusive of the special tax
3572 provided for in section 481 of the Home Rule Act pledged to payment of general obligation
3573 indebtedness of the District.
3574 (3) “Available Sales Tax Revenues” means the revenues resulting from the
3575 imposition of the tax under Chapter 20 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code,
168

3576 including penalty and interest charges, exclusive of the portion thereof required to be deposited
3577 in the Washington Convention Center Fund established pursuant to section 208 of the
3578 Washington Convention Center Authority Act of 1994, effective September 28, 1994 (D.C. Law
3579 10-188; D.C. Official Code § 10-1202.08), and any amounts to be made available to the
3580 Washington Metropolitan Transit Authority pursuant to section 7101 of the Fiscal Year 2018
3581 Budget Support Act of 2017, effective December 13, 2017 (D.C. Law 22-0033; 64 DCMR
3582 7652), and section 2 of the Stable and Reliable Source of WMATA Revenues Act of 1982,
3583 effective April 30, 1982 (D.C. Law 4-103; D.C. Official Code § 9-1111.15(b)(2)(A)).
3584 (4) “Available Tax Increment,” means the sum of the Available Sales Tax
3585 Revenues and Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Frank D. Reeves
3586 Municipal Center TIF Area in any fiscal year of the District minus the sum of Available Sales
3587 Tax Revenues and Available Real Property Tax Revenues generated in the Frank D. Reeves
3588 Municipal Center TIF Area in the applicable base year.
3589 (5) “Bond Counsel” means a firm or firms of attorneys designated as bond
3590 counsel from time to time by the Mayor.
3591 (6) “Bonds” means the District of Columbia revenue bonds, notes, or other
3592 obligations (including refunding bonds, notes, and other obligations), in one or more series,
3593 authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle.
3594 (7) “Chairman” means the Chairman of the Council of the District of Columbia.
3595 (8) “Chief Financial Officer” means the Chief Financial Officer established by
3596 section 424(a)(1) of the Home Rule Act.
3597 (9) “Closing Documents” means all documents and agreements, other than
3598 Financing Documents, that may be necessary and appropriate to issue, sell, and deliver the
169

3599 Bonds, and includes agreements, certificates, letters, opinions, forms, receipts, and other similar
3600 instruments.
3601 (10) “Council” means the Council of the District of Columbia.
3602 (11) “Debt Service” means principal, premium, if any, and interest on the Bonds.
3603 (12) “Development Costs” has the same meaning as in section 2(13) of the Tax
3604 Increment Financing Authorization Act of 1998, effective September 11, 1998 (D.C. Law 12-
3605 143; D.C. Official Code § 2-1217.01(13)).
3606 (13) “Development Sponsor” means Reeves CMC Venture, LLC, a District of
3607 Columbia limited liability company qualified to do business in the District of Columbia, or any
3608 other entity that undertakes the development of the project with the approval of the Mayor.
3609 (14) “District” means the District of Columbia.
3610 (15) “Financing Documents” means the documents, other than Closing
3611 Documents, that relate to the financing or refinancing of transactions to be affected through the
3612 issuance, sale, and delivery of the Bonds, including any offering document, and any required
3613 supplements to any such documents.
3614 (16) “Home Rule Act” means the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
3615 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 774; D.C. Official Code § 1-201.01 et seq.).
3616 (17) “Project” means the financing, refinancing, or reimbursing of Development
3617 Costs incurred within the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Area and adjoining parcels.
3618 (18) “Refunding Bonds” means the District of Columbia Bonds, notes, or other
3619 obligations, in one or more series, authorized to be issued pursuant to this subtitle to refund the
3620 Bonds.
3621 (19) “TIF” means tax increment financing.
170

3622 Sec. 7083. Creation of the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Fund.
3623 (a) There is established as a nonlapsing fund the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF
3624 Fund. The Chief Financial Officer shall deposit into the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF
3625 Fund the Available Tax Increment and any other taxes or fees specifically designated by law for
3626 deposit in the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Fund.
3627 (b) The Mayor may pledge and create a security interest in the funds in the Frank D.
3628 Reeves Municipal Center TIF Fund, or any sub-account within the Frank D. Reeves Municipal
3629 Center TIF Fund, for the payment of debt service on the Bonds without further action by the
3630 Council as permitted by section 490(f) of the Home Rule Act. The payment of debt service shall
3631 be made in accordance with the provisions of the Financing Documents entered into by the
3632 District in connection with the issuance of the Bonds.
3633 (c) If, at the end of any fiscal year of the District, the balance of cash and investments in
3634 the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Fund exceeds the amount of debt service (including
3635 prepayment of principal and interest), reserves on any Bonds, and any approved bond-related
3636 administrative expenses during the upcoming fiscal year, 50% of the excess shall be retained in
3637 the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Fund to prepay the principal of the Bonds or for
3638 future reserves or administrative expenses on the Bonds and the remaining 50% of the excess
3639 shall be transferred to the unrestricted balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia.
3640 Sec. 7084. Creation of the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Area.
3641 (a) There is created a TIF area designated as the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF
3642 Area, which shall consist of Lot 0844 in Square 0204 and Air Rights Lot 7000 in Square 0204 as
3643 shown on the tax rolls of the District as maintained by the Office of Tax and Revenue.
171

3644 (b) As provided in section 7083, the Available Tax Increment from the Frank D. Reeves
3645 Municipal Center TIF Area shall be deposited in the Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF
3646 Fund and may be used for the purposes set forth in section 7085.
3647 (c)(1) The base year for determination of Available Sales Tax Revenues shall be the tax
3648 year of the District preceding the tax year in which this subtitle becomes effective.
3649 (2) The base year for determination of Available Real Property Tax Revenues
3650 shall be the tax year of the District preceding the tax year in which this subtitle becomes
3651 effective and the initial assessed value to be used in making the determination of Available Real
3652 Property Tax Revenues shall be the assessed value of each lot of taxable real property in the
3653 Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Area for the tax year preceding the tax year in which this
3654 subtitle becomes effective.
3655 (d) The Frank D. Reeves Municipal Center TIF Area shall terminate on the earliest of:
3656 (1) December 31, 2057;
3657 (2) The date on which the Bonds are paid in full or are defeased and are no longer
3658 outstanding; and
3659 (3) December 31, 2032, if no Bonds are issued.
3660 Sec. 7085. Bond authorization.
3661 (a) The Council approves and authorizes the issuance of one or more series of Bonds in
3662 an aggregate principal amount not to exceed $32 million to fund the project. The Bonds, which
3663 may be issued from time to time, in one or more series, shall be tax-exempt or taxable as the
3664 Mayor shall determine and shall be payable and secured as provided in section 7086.
3665 (b) The proceeds of the Bonds shall be used to pay Development Costs of the Project,
3666 financing costs incurred by the District, and to fund capitalized interest and required reserves.
172

3667 (c) The Mayor may pay from the proceeds of the Bonds the financing costs and expenses
3668 of issuing and delivering the Bonds, including underwriting, legal, accounting, financial
3669 advisory, credit enhancement, marketing, sale, and printing costs and expenses.
3670 Sec. 7086. Payment and security.
3671 (a) Except as may be otherwise provided in this subtitle, the principal of, premium, if
3672 any, and interest on, the Bonds, and the payment of ongoing administrative expenses related to
3673 the bond financing shall be payable solely from proceeds received from the sale of the Bonds,
3674 income realized from the temporary investment of those proceeds, Available Tax Increment and
3675 other taxes and fees specifically designated by law for deposit into the Frank D. Reeves
3676 Municipal Center TIF Fund, income realized from the temporary investment of those receipts
3677 and revenues prior to payment to the Bond owners, and other funds that, as provided in the
3678 Financing Documents, may be made available to the District for payment of the Bonds from
3679 sources other than the District, all as provided for in the Financing Documents.
3680 (b) Payment of the Bonds shall be secured as provided in the Financing Documents and
3681 by an assignment by the District for the benefit of the Bond owners of certain of its rights under
3682 the Financing Documents and Closing Documents to the trustee for the Bonds pursuant to the
3683 Financing Documents.
3684 (c) The trustee or paying agent is authorized to deposit, invest, and disburse the proceeds
3685 received from the sale of the Bonds pursuant to the Financing Documents.
3686 Sec. 7087. Bond details.
3687 (a) The Mayor is authorized to take any action reasonably necessary or appropriate in
3688 accordance with this subtitle in connection with the preparation, execution, issuance, sale,
173

3689 delivery, security for, and payment of the Bonds of each class and series, including

3694 Bonds;
3695 (3) The rate or rates of interest or the method for determining the rate or rates of
3696 interest on the Bonds;
3697 (4) The date or dates of issuance, sale, and delivery of, and the payment of interest
3698 on, the Bonds, and the maturity date or dates of the Bonds;
3699 (5) The terms under which the Bonds may be paid, optionally or mandatorily
3700 redeemed, accelerated, tendered, called, or put for redemption, repurchase, or remarketing before

3723 (d) The official seal of the District, or a facsimile of it, shall be impressed, printed, or
3724 otherwise reproduced on the Bonds.

3726 instrument to be entered into by the District and a trustee or paying agent to be selected by the

3729 (f) The Bonds may be issued at any time or from time to time in one or more issues and
3730 in one or more series.
3731 (g) The Bonds are declared to be issued for essential public and governmental purposes.

3833 SUBTITLE H. NATIONAL COUNCIL OF NEGRO WOMEN, INC. REAL
3834 PROPERTY TAX EXEMPTION
3835 Sec. 7101. Short title.
3836 This subtitle may be cited as the “National Council of Negro Women, Inc., Real Property
3837 Tax Exemption Act of 2026”.
3838 Sec. 7102. Chapter 10 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
3839 follows:
3840 (a) The table of contents is amended by adding a new section designation to read as
3841 follows:
3842 “Sec. 47-1099.16. National Council of Negro Women, Inc.; Square 460, Lot 810.”.
3843 (b) A new section 47-1099.16 is added to read as follows:

4047 “§ 47-1803.04. Gross income — Individual, estate, and trust deductions.
4048 “(a) Deductions allowed — Generally.
4049 “(1) Individuals. An individual is allowed either the standard deduction or
4050 itemized deductions (including the additional deductions set forth in subsection (e) of this
4051 section, if applicable) as set forth in this section.
189

4052 “(2) Estates and Trusts. An estate or trust is allowed the itemized deductions
4053 (including the additional deductions set forth in subsection (e) of this section, if applicable) and
4054 any deductions allowed under § 47-1809.05.
4055 “(b) Standard deduction. If an individual elects to claim the standard deduction on the
4056 individual’s federal income tax return, the individual must claim the standard deduction as
4057 defined in § 47-1801.04(44), and no itemized deductions and other additions to the standard
4058 deduction are allowed, except as otherwise provided in this chapter. If an individual elects to
4059 claim any itemized deductions on the individual’s federal return, the individual must claim the
4060 itemized deductions as allowed under this section and the standard deduction is not allowed. For
4061 married individuals or domestic partners, if the net income of one of the spouses or registered
4062 domestic partners is determined by itemizing deductions on a separate return, neither of the
4063 spouses or registered domestic partners is allowed the standard deduction.
4064 “(c) Itemized deductions.
4065 “(1) Except as otherwise provided in this section, in computing net income, an
4066 individual, estate, or trust is allowed the following deductions:
4067 “(A) Any deduction allowed under the Internal Revenue Code of 1986,
4068 and to the same extent, on a federal individual or fiduciary income tax return; except, that a
4069 deduction for state or local taxes under § 164 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 (except as
4070 otherwise provided in subsection (d)(1) and (2) of this section) is allowed without regard to the
4071 applicable limitation amounts set forth in § 164(b)(6) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986.
4072 “(2)(A) In the case of an individual whose District of Columbia adjusted gross
4073 income exceeds the applicable amount, the amount of the itemized deductions otherwise
190

4074 allowable for the taxable year shall be reduced by 5% of the excess of the District of Columbia
4075 adjusted gross income over the applicable amount.
4076 “(B) For the purposes of this paragraph, the term:
4077 “(i) “Applicable amount” means $200,000 ($100,000, married
4078 filing separately); and
4079 “(ii) “Itemized deductions” does not include the deduction:
4080 “(I) Under § 213 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986
4081 relating to expenses such as, for example, medical or dental;
4082 “(II) For investment interest, as defined in § 163(d) of the
4083 Internal Revenue Code of 1986; and
4084 “(III) Under § 165(a) of the Internal Revenue Code of
4085 1986, for casualty or theft losses described in § 165(c)(2) and (3) of the Internal Revenue Code
4086 of 1986, or for losses described in § 165(d) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986.
4087 “(C) This subsection shall be applied after the application of any other
4088 limitation on the allowance of any itemized deduction.
4089 “(D) This subsection shall not apply to any estate or trust.
4090 “(d) Deductions not allowed. No deductions shall be allowed for the following:
4091 “(1) Income taxes;
4092 “(2) Franchise taxes imposed by this chapter;
4093 “(3) S corporation income. Any deduction passing to a stockholder in a small
4094 business corporation as defined in § 1371 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954, making an
4095 election under § 1372(a) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954, or an S Corporation as defined in
4096 § 1361(a) and (b) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, making an election under § 1362(a) of
191

4097 the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, that is otherwise deductible under the provisions of
4098 subsection (a) of this section and that was allowable in determining the taxable income of the
4099 small business corporation or S Corporation subject to tax under the provisions of subchapter VII
4100 of this chapter;
4101 “(4) Qualified business income. A deduction allowed under § 63(b)(3) or § 199A
4102 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986;
4103 “(5) Business deductions. Any deduction not allowed under § 47-1803.03 or in
4104 excess of a deduction allowed but limited under § 47-1803.03;
4105 “(6) Qualified tips. Any deduction allowed for qualified tips under § 224 of the

4110 “(8) Personal car loan interest. Any deduction for personal car loan interest

4217 SUBTITLE L. UNITED MEDICAL CENTER CLOSEOUT FUND
4218 Sec. 7141. Short title.
4219 This subtitle may be cited as the “United Medical Center Closeout Fund Establishment
4220 Act of 2026”.
4221 Sec. 7142. The Not-for-Profit Hospital Corporation Establishment Amendment Act of
4222 2011, effective September 14, 2011 (D.C. Law 19-21; D.C. Official Code § 44-951.01 et seq.), is
4223 amended by adding a new section 5131 to read as follows:
4224 “Sec. 5131. Hospital Closeout Fund.
4225 “(a) There is established as a special fund the United Medical Center Closeout Fund
4226 (“Fund”), which shall be administered by the Chief Financial Officer in accordance with
4227 subsection (c) of this section.
4228 “(b) The following revenue shall be deposited into the Fund:
4229 “(1) Funds of the Corporation;
4230 “(2) Funds of the hospital;
4231 “(3) Payments of accounts receivable to the Corporation or hospital;
4232 “(4) Payments to the Corporation or hospital from third-party payers;
197

4233 “(5) All other funds received by or on behalf of the Corporation or the hospital.
4234 “(c)(1) Money in the Fund may be used for:
4235 “(A) All purposes related to the closeout of the hospital, including
4236 collections or payments resulting from audits or other third-party reconciliations; and
4237 “(B) Any required expenses of the Corporation or hospital, including
4238 records management.
4239 “(2) Additionally, $10.918 million from the Fund shall be transferred to the
4240 General Fund of the District of Columbia in Fiscal Year 2027.
4241 “(d)(1) The money deposited into the Fund but not expended in a fiscal year shall not
4242 revert to the unassigned fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia at the end
4243 of a fiscal year, or at any other time, except as provided in subsections (c)(2) and (e) of this
4244 section.
4245 “(2) Subject to authorization in an approved budget and financial plan, any funds
4246 appropriated in the Fund shall be continually available without regard to fiscal year limitation.
4247 “(e) Any money remaining available in the Fund after all obligations of the Corporation
4248 and the hospital have been settled or paid, as determined by the Chief Financial Officer, shall be
4249 transferred to the unassigned fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as
4250 part of the fiscal year-end close for the year in which such determination is made by the Chief
4251 Financial Officer.”
4252 Sec. 7143. Applicability.
4253 This subtitle shall apply as of October 1, 2025.

REFERENCE: Draft bill as provided to the Office of Revenue Analysis on April 10,
2026
Conclusion
Funds are sufficient in the fiscal year 2027 through fiscal year 2030 budget and financial plan to
implement the Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026. The budget and financial plan accounts
for the expenditure and revenue implications of the bill.
The bill, the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” is the legislative vehicle for adopting
statutory changes needed to implement the District’s proposed budget and financial plan for the fiscal
years 2027 through 2030. The following pages summarize the purpose and the impact of each subtitle.

TITLE I – GOVERNMENT DIRECTION AND SUPPORT
Subtitle (I)(A) – Telework Policy Amendment Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle requires the Mayor to establish a telework policy for all agencies, except the Council and
agencies of the legislative branch, and prohibits District personnel authorities from establishing a
different telework policy without authorization from the Mayor. The subtitle also requires every
agency to submit a report to the Mayor with information on the use of telework by employees, and it
authorizes the Mayor to audit agency implementation of the telework policy.
The subtitle also prohibits personnel authorities from entering into a collective bargaining
agreement that includes or requires a telework policy.
Financial Plan Impact
The subtitle does not impact the budget and financial plan.
Subtitle (I)(B) - Limitations on Liability Against the District of Columbia Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle places limits on the District’s unliquidated damages liability to persons or property
resulting from actions by the District government. The subtitle limits damages to $500,000 for all
claimants related to a single incident or occurrence. The limit is $1 million if the damages were
awarded due to intentional wrongful acts or omissions by the District. The subtitle requires any
defendant to expend more than $10,000 in medical expenses to be eligible for an award for
noneconomic damages, except in cases of permanent disfigurement or death emanating from an
intentional wrongful act. These limits apply to any case filed in court or another relevant tribunal on
or after October 1, 2026.
Financial Plan Impact
In fiscal year 2025 the District exceeded its initial annual budget for settlements and judgments by
nearly $20 million. The subtitle will limit the District’s potential exposure to claims. While each claim
against the District is unique, establishing payment limits will limit the District’s overall potential
claims exposure. As a result, amounts budgeted for settlements and judgments have been reduced by
$22.5 million in savings over the four-year financial plan period starting in fiscal year 2028.
Subtitle I(B) - Limitations on Liability Against the District of Columbia Act of 2026
Settlements and Judgements Savings

Annual Savings $0 $7,500 $7,500 $7,500 $22,500

Subtitle (I)(C) – District Employee Paid Parental, Family, and Medical Leave Amendment Act
of 2026
Background
The subtitle changes eligibility requirements and available benefits for the paid parental, family and
medical leave program for District government employees.
First, the subtitle requires a District government employee to be employed by the District for at least
180 continuous days to be eligible.
Second, employees must provide written notice to their agency describing the need for the leave and
provide a schedule of expected hours during which the employee intends to take the leave. The notice
must be provided at least ten days in advance, if the leave is foreseeable. If the leave is due to an
unforeseeable event, the employee must provide details of the leave either orally or in writing within
48 hours after the emergency occurs. The subtitle allows for a good faith negotiation on dates for
taking leave and allows an agency to deny use of paid leave if an employee does not agree to a
reasonable request to revise the dates.
Third, the subtitle removes grandparents and siblings from the list of defined family members for
which family care leave may be taken.
Fourth, the subtitle reduces the maximum leave that can be taken when caring for a defined family
member for qualifying family leave events from eight weeks per year to two.
Fifth, the subtitle requires probationary employees to enter into a continuation of service agreement
to stay on as an employee for at least 12 weeks after the use of paid parental, family or medical leave.
Probationary employees who voluntarily separate prior to the end of a continuation of service
agreement will be considered indebted to the District government for salary paid during the leave
period.
Financial Plan Impact
At some agencies and for certain positions, family care leave can require agencies to cover absences
of essential employees by using overtime of other employees. An analysis of fiscal year 2025 family
care hours taken by employees of ten selected agencies1 shows that the subtitle’s restriction of family
care to two weeks would have resulted in 177,000 hours of reduced paid family care leave . It is
estimated that about half of these hours will still be taken, however, utilizing other employee leave
options such an unpaid Family and Medical Leave Act usage. The other half of reduced leave-taking
hours is projected to result in a corresponding reduction of overtime expenses . This is estimated to
save $5.7 million across ten agencies in fiscal year 2027 and $23.7 million across the four-year
financial plan.
1 Agencies selected for cost analysis were Child and Family Services Agency, Department of Behavioral Health,
Department of General Services, Department of Corrections, Department of Human Services, Department of
Public Works, Department of Youth Rehabilitation Services, Fire and Emergency Management Services,
Metropolitan Police Department, and Office of Unified Communications.

Subtitle (I)(D) – Lobbyist Late Filing Penalty Amendment Act of 2026
Background
District law2 stipulates that any person who files a required lobbyist report or registration form in
an untimely manner be assessed a civil penalty of $100 per day for up to 60 days, excluding weekends
and holidays. The Board of Government Ethics and Accountability (BEGA) may waive this for good
cause. The subtitle removes3 the exclusion for weekends and holidays and makes the 60-day time
frame consecutive.
Financial Plan Impact
The subtitle does not have an impact on the budget and financial plan. The subtitle allows BEGA to
impose late filing fines in a timelier manner without overlapping into the next filing period. BEGA
utilizes an e-filing system, which is available on the website 24/7, for lobbyists to file their
registrations and activity reports.BEGA will continue to process reports and registrations, and assess
penalties, with resources budgeted in the fiscal year 2027 budget and financial plan.
Subtitle (I)(E) – Mayoral Transition Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle authorizes the Mayor to take “appropriate action” to assure continuity in a change of
administrations. It authorizes the current Mayor to spend up to $300,000 to provide resources and
support to the next Mayor-elect and his or her transition staff, including: office space, furniture,
machines, supplies, compensation to transition staff, and other reasonable expenses.
Financial Plan Impact
The Non-Departmental Account (Agency DO0) has up to $300,000 available for transition expenses
in fiscal year 2027.
2 D.C. Official Code § 1-1162.32(c).
3 By amending the Board of Ethics and Government Accountability Establishment and Comprehensive Ethics
Reform Amendment Act of 2011, effective April 27, 2012 (D.C. Law 19-124; D.C. Official Code § 1-1162.32(c)).

Fiscal Impact Statement for the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” Draft bill as provided to Office
of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
Subtitle (I)(F) – Fair Elections Program Amendment Act of 2026
Background
The Fair Elections Program4, managed by the Office of Campaign Finance (OCF), provides for the
optional public funding of political campaigns in the District. Participation in the program is
voluntary, and participants must abide by contribution limits, expenditure prohibitions, and
reporting requirements. OCF is required to revoke the certification of a candidate participating in the
program if they do not comply with the program’s requirements, fail to qualify for the ballot, or cease
campaigning for the position for which they were certified.
The subtitle makes candidates personally liable for any expended base or matching funding the
candidate received, if the candidate’s certification is revoked, or if the candidate engages in
fraudulent activities. The Campaign Finance Board may reduce a participating candidate’s personal
liability if they terminate their candidacy for good cause including health reasons or personal
hardship. The subtitle explicitly states that good cause does not include electoral reasons such as low
standing in the polls, lack of fundraising success, or low expectation of electoral success.
Financial Plan Impact
OFT currently manages the revocation process for the program and initiates enforcement to recover
unexpended funds. The subtitle does not significantly burden that process and can be managed
within current resources.
4 D.C. Official Code § 1–1163.32a, et al. (https://ocf.dc.gov/page/overview-fair-elections-program)
Page 9 of 71

The Honorable Phil Mendelson
Fiscal Impact Statement for the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” Draft bill as provided to Office
of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
TITLE II – ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT AND REGULATION
Subtitle (II)(A) - Downtown Building Conversion Support Amendment Act of 2026
Background
The Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic Development (DMPED) manages two programs
designed to spur development in downtown Washington, D.C. The Housing in Downtown program5
encourages the transition of existing office buildings into residential buildings. The Office to Anything
program6 encourages the transition of unused or underutilized office buildings into new, activated
commercial, entertainment, retail, or non-residential uses. DMPED incentivizes participation in the
programs through real property tax abatements and freezes.
The Housing in Downtown program requires that affordable units included in the conversion project
comply with the District’s Inclusionary Zoning Program.7 The subtitle redefines bedroom to include
any habitable room that has a closet, is designated as a bedroom or sleeping room, and receives
natural light and ventilation, regardless of whether the room has access to an exterior window. This
definition applies to both affordable and market rate units and only to properties not otherwise
subject to the Inclusionary Zoning Program. The subtitle also repeals a requirement that property
owners contract with certified business enterprises for 35 percent of the operations of the
conversion project. Property owners must still contract with certified business enterprises for 35
percent of the contract dollar volume of the project’s construction elements.
The subtitle expands the Office to Anything program to include a conversion of any non-residential
building to any other non-residential use. The subtitle clarifies that the Mayor can cancel an eligibility
and reservation letter under the Office to Anything program for a failure to comply with any condition
established in the document. The subtitle authorizes the Mayor to terminate the eligibility for any
property if it fails to meet established conditions or offer a property owner the opportunity to cure
any deficiencies. If the property owner cures the deficiencies, the Mayor should not grant the tax
abatement during the period of deficiency and the fifteen-year period of the tax freeze should not be
tolled for the deficient period.
The subtitle exempts any projects in the Office to Anything program from the District’s First Source
requirements8 for the construction and development phases of the conversion project.
The subtitle applies the existing Building Conversion Permit Fee9 that is charged to projects under
the Housing in Downtown program to any projects participating in the Office to Anything program.
5 Tax Abatements for Housing in Downtown Amendment Act of 2022, effective September 21, 2022 (D.C. Law
24-167; D.C. Official Code § 47-860.01 et seq.).
6 Central Washington Activation Program Amendment Act of 2024, effective September 18, 2024 (D.C. Law 25-
217; D.C. Official Code § 47-870 et seq.).
7 Inclusionary Zoning Implementation Amendment Act of 2006, effective March 14, 2007 (D.C. Law 16-275;
D.C. Official Code § 6-1041.01 et seq.). and Inclusionary Zoning, effective May 3, 2025 (11 DCMR § 11-C10).
8 First Source Employment Agreement Act of 1984, effective June 29, 1984 (D.C. Law 5-93; D.C. Official Code §
2-219.03).
9 Building Permit Fees, effective December 6, 2025 (12-M DCMR § 101.1(a-1)).
Page 10 of 71

The Honorable Phil Mendelson
Fiscal Impact Statement for the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” Draft bill as provided to Office
of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
Financial Plan Impact
The subtitle’s changes to the Housing in DC program that alter the definition of a bedroom and change
the certified business enterprises contracting commitment will ease the regulatory burdens for
projects seeking inclusion in the program. However, these changes are not expected to significantly
increase the number of projects seeking program approval.
Since the Office to Anything program’s inception in fiscal year 2025, only two to three projects have
shown interest in the program. The subtitle’s applicability of building conversion fees to Office to
Anything program participants means that program participants will pay lower building permit fees
than they would otherwise pay for a conversion. However, the limited interest in the program,
combined with growth from the program’s expansion, less restrictive First Source requirements, and
lower fees, should generate additional building permit fee revenues to offset any potential losses
from the change in the building permit fee applicability. The program’s real property tax abatements
remain capped at $5 million in fiscal year 2027, $6 million in fiscal year 2028, $8 million in fiscal year
2029, and 104 percent of the prior year’s cap beginning in fiscal year 2030.
Subtitle (II)(B) – Rent Payment Reporting Amendment Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle authorizes the Mayor to establish a rent payment reporting program (“Program”), which
will be managed by the Department of Housing and Community Development (DHCD). The Program
will facilitate providing information from rental housing providers about a tenant’s rent payment
history to consumer credit bureaus. Tenants must authorize participation in the Program and the
transfer of their payment information.
The Mayor may issue grants to rental housing providers to help cover costs associated with
participating in the Program and require providers who receive financial support to participate.
Financial Plan Impact
DHCD’s budget has $500,000 set aside in recurring funding for the program. This is the estimated
cost of a third-party provider to manage the program.

Subtitle (II)(C) – Workforce Housing Opportunity Amendment Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle creates a new real property tax abatement program for a residential development of at
least 40 units. Developers with projects seeking the tax abatement must apply to, and be certified by,
Page 11 of 71

The Honorable Phil Mendelson
Fiscal Impact Statement for the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” Draft bill as provided to Office
of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
the Mayor. Applications must include a third-party fiscal analysis demonstrating that the project is
only feasible with the tax abatement. Projects must meet affordability requirements to be awarded,
and to maintain, the tax abatement. At least 20 percent of the units must be affordable at the level
of 80% of median family income, and at least 20 percent must be affordable at 100% of median family
income. Certified Business Enterprises must receive thirty-five percent of development and
operating costs, and the developer must enter into a First Source Agreement. The Mayor may use a
competitive process to award the tax abatements and must limit the total value of abatements to $4
million in fiscal year 2029, $5 million in fiscal year 2030, and $6 million in fiscal year 2031.
Thereafter, the total value of abatements under the program may grow at 5 percent annually.
Tax abatements begin with the project’s certificate of occupancy for all affordable units, and may end
after 20 years, provided that the Mayor determines a 20-year tax abatement is necessary for the
feasibility of the project. Otherwise, tax abatements provided to a project will last for ten years.
Financial Plan Impact
The subtitle will reduce real property tax revenue starting in fiscal year 2029. The Office of the
Deputy Mayor for Economic Development can review abatement applications and certify abatements
for the Office of Tax and Revenue. The total cost of the subtitle is $9 million through 2030.

Subtitle (II)(D) – Federal Property Development Tax Incentive Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle authorizes the Mayor to approve a real property tax exemption for certain properties
disposed by the Federal government after October 1, 2026. Such properties may have been disposed
by sale or ground lease to the District government, or by sale or ground lease to a private entity. If
disposed to the District government, the property may be further transferred by sale or ground lease
to a private entity. The properties must be subject to a development plan that will result in the
development of at least 200,000 square feet of gross floor area and must not have been subject to
real property tax or payment in lieu of taxes10 prior. The developer must enter into an agreement to:
• Contract with certified business enterprises for at least 35% of the contract dollar
volume of the construction and development of the project;
• Enter into a First Source Agreement for the construction and development of the
project;
• Maintain, for the duration of the tax abatement, at least 10% of the housing units
developed or redeveloped on the real property as affordable to households earning
on average 60% or less of the median family income;
10 § 47-811 or § 47-1005.01
Page 12 of 71

The Honorable Phil Mendelson
Fiscal Impact Statement for the “Fiscal Year 2027 Budget Support Act of 2026,” Draft bill as provided to Office
of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
• Offer at least 10% of the housing units offered for sale at a price affordable to
households earning on average 80% or less of the median family income; and
• Agree to such other terms and conditions as the Mayor considers appropriate.
Further conditions for the Mayor to provide the tax abatement include that the Mayor considers the
project to be of special merit; that the tax abatement is necessary to make the project financially
feasible; and that the developer has the ability to complete the project in a timely manner. The Mayor
may provide the tax abatements for a period to last up to 20 years. The tax abatement may begin in
the tax year commencing after the tax year in which the certificate of occupancy was issued for the
development on the property.
Financial Plan Impact
The subtitle is not projected to reduce real property tax revenue in the financial plan period.
Property tax revenue over the last five years, which form the base for revenue estimates, do not
include over- 200,000 square-foot developments from previously Federally-owned properties
except for developments required to be supported with subsidies such as PILOT bonds. This type of
development is therefore not a component of forecasted property tax revenue over the financial plan
period. The requirements for the abatement would also preclude any development projects that
would be financially feasible without an abatement, including projects that would only include
market-rate housing. Moreover, current development conditions also mean that tax abatement start
dates would occur outside of the financial plan period.
The Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic Development can, using its budgeted resources, enter
into the agreements required of developers receiving the tax abatement and certify properties to the
Office of Tax and Revenue that should receive the abatement.
Subtitle (II)(E) – WMATA Joint Development Properties Tax Abatement Act of 2026
Background
The subtitle authorizes the Mayor to provide real property tax abatements for certain joint
development properties located within 1750 feet of a Metrorail station. Requirements include that
the Mayor determines the abatement is necessary for the project to be financially feasible and the
project is of special merit; and that the developer enters into a First Source agreement and uses
Certified Business Enterprises. Additionally, ten percent of any residential units must be set aside as
affordable at the 60% of median income level, and an additional ten percent at 80% of median income
level, for the duration of the tax abatement. The duration of the tax abatement begins with certificate
of occupancy and may last for a maximum of 20 years, provided that the Mayor determines the
duration necessary for the project to be financially feasible. The developer must make substantial
progress on the development within 5 years.
Financial Plan Impact
WMATA has potentially eligible development sites at the Takoma, Friendship Heights, Fort Totten
and Deanwood rail stations. Of these, the Takoma and Deanwood sites are projected to have
development that would occur within the financial plan period. The estimated value of the
abatements provided by the subtitle is $108,000 in fiscal year 2027 and a total of $3.1 million over

of Revenue Analysis, April 10, 2026
the financial plan. The Deputy Mayor for Planning and Economic Development and the Office of Tax
